<sup class="footnote-marker">223</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 53a, <i>Sifra Aḥare Pereq</i> 3(11).</i> It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">224</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:12–13.</i> <i>and he shall bring it inside the curtain, and put the incense in the fire before the Eternal,</i> that he should not prepare outside and bring inside, since the Sadducees are saying, he shall prepare outside and then bring inside. If one does this before flesh and blood, <i>a fortiori</i> before the Omnipresent. Also it says<sup class="footnote-marker">225</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:2.</i>, <i>for in a cloud I shall appear over the cover.</i> The Sages said to them, has it not already been said, <i>he shall put the incense in the fire before the Eternal;</i> only inside he puts it on. If it is so, why was it said, <i>for in a cloud I shall appear over the cover</i>? This teaches that he has to put in smoke-creating herb. From where that he has to add smoke-creating herb? The verse says<sup class="footnote-marker">226</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:13.</i>, <i>the incense shall cover the cover over the chest</i><sup class="footnote-marker">227</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s misquote.</i>,<i>lest he die.</i> If he failed to add smoke-creating herb or left out any of its ingredients he has committed a deadly sin<sup class="footnote-marker">228</sup><i class="footnote">Babli <i>Keritut</i> 6a.</i>. <i>Lest he die,</i> that is the punishment. <i>For in a cloud I</i> shall appear over the cover, this is the warning.
<sup class="footnote-marker">229</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Sifra A hare Introduction</i> (13).</i> Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Simeon said, I could think that punishment and warning had been said before the death of the two sons of Aaron, the verse says<sup class="footnote-marker">230</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:1.</i>, <i>after the death of the two sons of Aaron.</i> If <i>after the death of the two sons of Aaron.</i> I could think that both had been said after the death of the two sons of Aaron, the verse says, <i>for in a cloud I shall appear over the cover.</i> How is that? The warning was said before the death of the two sons of Aaron, but the punishment was said after the death of the two sons of Aaron, Rebbi Zeˋura said, it does not say “because in a cloud I was seen over the cover,” but <i>I shall be seen.</i> From here that the Holy One, praise to Him, does not punish unless he had warned<sup class="footnote-marker">231</sup><i class="footnote">The tannaitic position is rejected. While the death of the two sons of Aaron made an atonement ceremony necessary, their deaths cannot be punishment for infractions of laws not yet promulgated.</i>.

Halakhah 6

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If he was a scholar, he preaches<sup class="footnote-marker">232</sup><i class="footnote">Explains biblical verses either legalistically or as homilies.</i>; otherwise scholars preach before him. If he was used to reciting<sup class="footnote-marker">233</sup><i class="footnote">As technical term, קורא always means reading biblical texts with the masoretic accents. (which in those times were not written but had to be memorized.)</i> he recites; otherwise one recites before him. What does one recite before him? Job, Ezra, and Chronicles. Zacariah ben Qebutal says, many times I recited before him from Daniel.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> It was stated, in Proverbs and Psalms, since their interest makes sleep disappear.
Cahana asked Rav, how shall we state, Qebutar or Qebutal<sup class="footnote-marker">234</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 19b; there the question is not between <i>r</i> and <i>l</i> but between <i>b</i> and <i>p</i> with opposite readings in the printed edition and the Munich ms.</i>? He was standing in prayer and indicated to him by his finger, a bird, <i>kabōtar</i><sup class="footnote-marker">235</sup><i class="footnote">“Dove”. <i>kabōtar</i> in Pahlevi, كبوتر <i>kabūtar</i> in Farsi.</i><i>.</i>

Halakhah 7

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> If he became sleepy, the young priests drum before him with a dry finger and say to him, Sir High Priest, stand up and take it easy once on the floor. One occupies him until the time of slaughter.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rav Ḥuna said, “with a dry finger” orally. But Rebbi Joḥanan said, “with a dry finger”, with the hand. A <i>baraita</i> disagrees with Rebbi Joḥanan “orally, not with harp nor with lute.<sup class="footnote-marker">236</sup><i class="footnote">Tosephta 1:9, Babli 19b.</i>” He explains it, the melody indicated by the dry finger one says orally, not with harp nor with lute.

Halakhah 8

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Every day one removes ashes from the altar<sup class="footnote-marker">237</sup><i class="footnote">The removal of the ashes from the previous day is the required action before the service of the new day may start; <i>Lev.</i>6:1–6.</i> about at the call of the cock, before it or after it. But on the Day of Atonement at midnight<sup class="footnote-marker">238</sup><i class="footnote">To let the High Priest start the office of the day at the earliest possible moment.</i>, and on holidays after the first watch<sup class="footnote-marker">239</sup><i class="footnote">The end of the first third of the night. On holidays not only were there many additional public offerings but also a very great number of private holiday offerings' taking up the entire day.</i>. The cock did not crow<sup class="footnote-marker">240</sup><i class="footnote">On holidays and the Day of Atonement.</i> before the Courtyard was full of Israel.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rebbi Mana said, would it not be understandable if on the day of Atonement it were after the first watch and on holidays from midnight, that they<sup class="footnote-marker">241</sup><i class="footnote">Everybody involved in the service of the fast day. R. Mana’s opinion is not mentioned in the Babli.</i> should not become thirsty? Rebbi Joḥanan said, the removal of ashes is the start of the service of the next say and one had to sanctify his hands and feet from the basin which was immersed in water<sup class="footnote-marker">242</sup><i class="footnote">Washing hands and feet before any sacral act is an absolute requirement, <i>Ex.</i>30:17–21. But the water used on one day would become unusable the next day unless it is at least 40 <i>seˋah,</i> the minimum volume of a <i>miqweh</i> whose water always is pure. Therefore the wash basin of the priests has to be immersed in a large <i>miqweh</i> during the night and can be lifted for easy use only at dawn. For the removal of ashes on the special days, hands and feet have to be washed in the <i>miqweh.</i> In the interpretation of the Babli <i>Zevaḥim</i> 21b, R. Joḥanan holds that since the removal of the ashes is the start of the service of the next day, the Cohen washing for the removal does not have to wash again for the morning service.</i>.

Chapter 2



Halakhah 1

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Originally, anybody who wanted to remove the ashes<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">The ritual removal of some ashes from the altar by a priest in special attire <i>(Lev.</i>6:3), followed by the less formal removal of the remainder of the ashes, <i>Lev.</i> 6:4.</i> from the altar could remove them. If they were many of them, they ran up the ramp<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">The ramp on the South side of the altar, leading to the top without stairs <i>(Ex.</i>20:23).</i>; he who was first within four cubits<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">4 cubits from the top of the altar.</i> got the right to do it. If two were at equal times, the overseer used to say to them, show fingers<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">Since people may not be counted, one counts fingers instead. The overseer calls out a large number and then counts down finger by finger repeatedly and the person whose finger is then number 1 is selected. (In modern Hebrew, מצביע no longer means to show a finger, or to point with a finger, but “to vote”; a misinterpretation of this Mishnah..)</i>. What do they hold up? One or two<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">If a Cohen has arthritic fingers and cannot lift a single finger, he may show two which, being close to one another, will be counted as one.</i>; but one does not show a thumb in the Temple<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">Since the thumb is far from the other fingers, the thumb and one other finger might erroneously be counted as two persons.</i>.<br>It happened that two were equally running up the ramp when one pushed the other who broke his leg. When the court saw that they might come into danger they enacted that they should remove the ashes from the altar only by lottery<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">Since people may not be counted, one counts fingers instead. The overseer calls out a large number and then counts down finger by finger repeatedly and the person whose finger is then number 1 is selected. (In modern Hebrew, מצביע no longer means to show a finger, or to point with a finger, but “to vote”; a misinterpretation of this Mishnah..)</i>. There were four lotteries, and this was the first of them.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “Originally, anybody who wanted to remove the ashes from the altar,” etc. Rebbi Mana asked, why did they not establish a lottery for the removal of ashes? Come and see, slaughter is valid by a non-Cohen, but you are saying that there is a lottery<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah 2:2.</i>. Removal of ashes is forbidden to a non-Cohen, and you are saying, there is no lottery? Rebbi Mana turned around and said, slaughter is valid only during daytime, but the removal of ashes is valid during the entire night. If you are saying that there is a lottery, he will not get up early for the doubt<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">If the chances are slim that he will be able to serve, no Cohen will show up for the night duty. Babli 22a.</i>. What did you see to say this? <i>All the night</i><sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 6:2.</i><i>, he shall remove</i><sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 6:3.</i><i>.</i> From here that the removal of ashes is valid during the entire night.
A non-Cohen who removed<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">The formal removal of ashes from the altar.</i>. Rebbi Joḥanan said, he is liable. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, he is not liable. What is Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish’s reason? <i>Service of bringing</i><sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Num.</i> 18:7.</i><i>.</i> This excludes what is a removal. What is Rebbi Joḥanan ’s reason? <i>Anything concerning the altar</i><sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Num.</i> 18:7.</i><i>.</i> Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun in the name of Rav: The four kinds of service for which a Cohen would be liable if done outside<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">Outside a divinely approved place of worship; after the building of the Temple, outside of the Temple district. Worship outside the Temple is sinful only if it imitates Temple ceremonies. Babli 24a.</i>, the non-Cohen is liable for inside. What are these? Burning incense, and pouring blood, and making libations of water and wine. This follows Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish. Levi said, even removal of the ashes;<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 24a.</i> this follows Rebbi Joḥanan. If he<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">The non-Cohen.</i> stirred the coals, the disagreement of Rebbi Joḥanan and Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish. If he<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">The non-Cohen.</i> removed the remainder of the ashes, the disagreement of Rebbi Joḥanan and Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish, following him who said, <i>others</i><sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 6:4. <i>Sifra Ṣaw Pereq</i> 2(6).</i>, of lesser value than these. But for him<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">According to <i>Sifra,</i> R. Eleazar (the Tanna.)</i> who said <i>others,</i> to include people with bodily defects, there is no difference between a Cohen with a bodily defect and a non-Cohen. Everybody agreed that the non-Cohen who arranged the woods<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">The logs of firewood on the altar.</i> is liable. Rebbi Zeˋira said, but only for the two logs on which the verse insists that they are Cohen’s service: <i>Aaron’s the priest’s</i> <i>sons shall put fire on the altar and arrange woods</i><sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 1:7. Since a simple plural always means 2 (Note 138); this establishes a formal requirement that two new logs be brought to the altar at the start of the morning service; <i>Lev.</i> 6:5. Babli 24b.</i><i>.</i>
It was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Sifra Ṣaw Pereq</i> 2(7).; Babli 24b,45a.</i> “Rebbi Jehudah said, from where that kindling fire wood<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">Rashi’s explanation.</i> may only be done by a qualified Cohen and with a vessel of service<sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote">The firewood had to be transported in a dedicated vessel.</i>? The verse says, <i>Aaron’s the priest’s sons shall put fire on the altar.</i> Rebbi Simeon said, could anybody think that a non-Cohen might approach the top of the altar? Then why is it said, <i>Aaron’s the priest’s sons shall put fire on the altar?</i> This teaches that kindling the fire may only be done on top of the altar” They objected, is it not written <i>“and the fire on the altar shall burn there, it shall not go out</i><sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 6:5.</i><i>,</i> from here that kindling the fire may only be done on top of the altar, the words of Rebbi Jehudah<sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 45a.</i>”? The argument of Rebbi Jehudah is inverted. There it needs a qualified Cohen, but here it does not need a qualified Cohen. Rebbi Tanḥum bar Yudan said, what do you understand from here? Could we say on top of the altar and a non-Cohen<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote">Since it already was stated that no non-Cohen could be present at the altar, a mention of “Cohen” was superfluous in the second case.</i>?
If he removed and the wind blew it away<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote">Does one have to lift a second time?</i>, the disagreement between Rebbi Joḥanan and Rebbi Ḥanina, since Rebbi Ḥanina said, if a fistful<sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote">A flour offering after dedication is most holy, all use is forbidden as larceny of <i>sancta.</i> The priest has to take a fistful of the flour mixed with oil, bring it to the top of the altar in a dedicated vessel, and empty the vessel into the fire. At that moment, the owners have fulfilled their vow, and the remainders of the offering are released to the priests as their property, to be eaten in the sacred precinct.</i> was put in the fire when the wind blew it away, by the last blowing the owner was atoned for and the remainders freed from larceny. Rebbi Joḥanan said, if<sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning; <i>only if.</i> Babli <i>Menaḥot</i>26b.</i> the fire engulfed most of it. What means “most of it”? Most of the fistful, or had it been said about most of each separate lump? There came Rebbi Ḥizqiah, Rebbi Jonah, Rebbi Abba, Rebbi Ḥiyya, in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: It had been said about most of each separate lump.
If he lifted half of it, the disagreement between Rebbi Joḥanan and Rebbi Joshua ben Levi, since Rebbi Joḥanan said, if the fistful had been sanctified in a vessel, he did his duty if he burned even a sesame grain’s size of it. Rebbi Joshua ben Levi said, the Mishnah<sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Menaḥot</i>3:4, Babli <i>Menaḥot</i>26a.</i> does not say so, only if he burned his fistful in two parts it is qualified. Rebbi Ḥama bar Uqba in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi: A fistful is not less than the volume of two olives, no burning is less than the volume of (a fistful) [an olive]<sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Menaḥot</i>26b. The corrector’s change is suspect as adaptation to the Babli.</i>. Rebbi Isaac ben Rebbi Eleazar asked, then a Cohen whose hand could not hold the volume of two olives would be disqualified from the service<sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote">Since this disability does not appear in a list of defects which disqualify a Cohen, practice cannot follow R. Joshua ben Levi.</i>?
If he removed with his left hand, the disagreement between Rebbi Joḥanan and Jehudah ben Rebbi, since Rebbi Joḥanan said, if a fistful<sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote">Of the flour offering.</i> had been sanctified in a dedicated vessel and he burned it whether out of his hand or out of a vessel, whether by his right hand or by the left. Jehudah ben Rebbi said, either like a purification offering from the hand, or like a reparation offering from a vessel, but only with the right hand<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">In <i>Lev.</i> 6:10 it is stated that the flour offering is “most holy, like purification offering and like reparation offering.” For purification offerings it is stated (<i>Lev.</i>4:25, 30, 34) that the Cohen has to apply the blood of the sacrifice <i>with his finger</i> to the corners of the altar. This requirement is missing for the reparation sacrifice (<i>Lev.</i>7:1–7.)</i>. They objected: Was it not stated, if he received with his right hand and then put it into his left hand, he must return it to the right hand<sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Zevaḥim</i> 3:1, <i>Zevaḥim</i> 32a, speaking of the blood received in a vessel and brought to the altar to be poured at the wall.</i>? If from the left hand he returns it for the altar, not so much more to the cup? Rebbi La said, if somebody stated this, Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Simeon stated it. As it was stated, it<sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote">The fistful taken from a flour offering.</i> does not need sanctification in a cup. Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Simeon follows the argument of his father Rebbi Simeon, as we have stated there<sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Menaḥot</i>3:4.</i>, “not in a dedicated vessel it is disqualified, but Rebbi Simeon qualifies it.” How is it? The rabbis who require a dedicated vessel need the right hand<sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Menaḥot</i>26b.</i>; Rebbi Simeon [who] does not require a dedicated vessel does not need the right hand. Rebbi Mana said, I am wondering how the rabbis could compare the removal of ashes to burning, but it can be compared only to the lifting of the fistful, since both are by lifting<sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote">Since everybody agrees that at all places where the verse requires that the action be done by a Cohen he must use his right hand; therefore the lifting of the fistful must be with the Cohen’s right hand.</i>.
<i>And he shall lift</i><sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 6:3.</i>. There is no lifting unless he left a remainder<sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote">Otherwise the verse would have said, “he takes away”.</i>. <i>Which ate.</i> there is no eating less than the volume of an olive. If all of it<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote">The ashes on the altar.</i> was the volume of an olive? You may not take part of it since there would not be the volume of an olive; you may not take all of it since there would not be a remainder. <i>And he lifts … what the fire ate.</i> I could think wood, the verse says, the elevation sacrifice<sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote">The verse reads: <i>He shall lift the ashes from where the fire ate the elevation sacrifice on the altar.</i></i>. If elevation sacrifice, I could think limbs of an elevation sacrifice<sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote">Parts of the daily sacrifice which still are recognizable as such.</i>; the verse says, <i>what the fire ate.</i> How is this? He scoops up from what has been consumed in the middle<sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">Where it is most likely from the sacrifice, not the fire wood. <i>Sifra Ṣaw Pereq</i> 2(4).</i> and descends. It is an obligation to bring wood before fire, as it is said<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 1:7.</i>, <i>they shall arrange on the</i><i>fire,</i> He mentioned wood before fire. If one arranged before he removed, he throws down and removes, disassembles and removes<sup class="footnote-marker">46</sup><i class="footnote">Since it has been stated that the removal of ashes is first in the service of a new day, and arranging new logs precedes the morning daily sacrifice, any arrangement preceding the removal of ashes is simply addition to the preceding day’s service and may be undone for the new day. <i>Sifra Wayyiqra</i> I <i>Pereq</i> 5(11).</i>.
Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa said, Hilfai asked: What is the status of a fistful given on the setting of the night<sup class="footnote-marker">47</sup><i class="footnote">It is a biblical commandment that all leftovers from the service of a certain day have to be burned on the altar during the following night. Therefore the question has to be, what is the status of the next morning’s flour offering which was brought to the altar at dawn before the required new wood was formally brought to the altar after the removal of the previous day’s ashes.</i>? Rebbi Jeremiah said, Hilfai asked: What is the status of the public parts on the setting of the night<sup class="footnote-marker">48</sup><i class="footnote">The same question as before, only referring to the parts of the sacrificial animals brought before the ritual setting of new logs in the morning. The questions remain unanswered also in the Babli. <i>Menaḥot</i>26b.</i>? Is that not a <i>baratta?</i> Nothing precedes the daily sacrifice but incense<sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote">Since the daily sacrifice is scheduled בבוקר “in the morning (<i>Ex.</i> 29:39) but the incense בבוקר בבוקר “in the early morning (<i>Ex.</i> 30:7); cf. Halakhah 3:5. Babli <i>Pesaḥim</i>59a.</i>. The <i>baratta</i> as commandment, what he is asking is as impediment<sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote">Is the service invalid if the precedences indicated by the verses are not followed?</i>. Does the diadem cover up for impurity of the hands<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote">Since except for the biblically ordained washing (“sanctification”) of hands and feet at the start of a priest’s period of service (<i>Ex.</i> 30:20,40:31–32) the rules of impurity of hands are purely rabbinical, and hands are purified by immersion in a <i>miqweh,</i> not by sanctification from the basin. The (unanswered) question is whether the diadem covers also non-biblical infractions of the rules.</i>? Do hands become disqualified by leaving<sup class="footnote-marker">52</sup><i class="footnote">It is obvious that if a Cohen leaves the sacred precinct because he has finished his tour of duty, for the next tour he has to sanctify his hands and feet again. The question is whether his hands become rabbinically impure if he leaves the sacred precinct for a prescribed ritual act, such as depositing excess ashes outside the sacred domain.</i>? Is that not a <i>barattai</i> If he sanctified<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote">Since except for the biblically ordained washing (“sanctification”) of hands and feet at the start of a priest’s period of service (<i>Ex.</i> 30:20,40:31–32) the rules of impurity of hands are purely rabbinical, and hands are purified by immersion in a <i>miqweh,</i> not by sanctification from the basin. The (unanswered) question is whether the diadem covers also non-biblical infractions of the rules.</i> his hands and feet and they became impure, he immerses them and they are pure; if he left they did not become disqualified because of leaving. This comes following the one who said, an overnight stay does not disqualify hands. What is his problem? [But here] it is following him who said, an overnight stay disqualifies hands. Do hands become impure for missing time? Is that not a <i>baraita?</i> If he sanctified his hands and feet today for tomorrow’s service<sup class="footnote-marker">53</sup><i class="footnote">It seems that one has to complete the sentence: the sanctification is valid.</i>.
Rebbi Joḥanan said, the removal of ashes is the start of the service of the next day and one had to sanctify his hands and feet from the basin which was immersed in water<sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">Chapter 1, Note 241, Babli <i>Zevaḥim</i>20a.</i>. Rebbi Ḥiyya ben Joseph said, it was sufficient that the day deliver to the night<sup class="footnote-marker">55</sup><i class="footnote">Chapter 1, Note 82.</i>. The colleagues in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan , after he lifted it he put it<sup class="footnote-marker">56</sup><i class="footnote">The basin has to stay in the cistern any time it is not used during the night. According to R. Ḥiyya ben Joseph this should be necessary only at dusk and dawn. According to R. Joḥanan , the new day starts in the preceding night, with the preparation for lifting ashes.</i> back down. A <i>baraita</i> disagrees with Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Joseph. <sup class="footnote-marker">57</sup><i class="footnote">Tosephta 1:9, differently Tosephta <i>Menaḥot</i>1:13. In that text, Rebbi agrees with R. Eleazar ben R. Simeon. Babli <i>Zevaḥim</i> 20b.</i>“If he sanctified his hands and feet during the day, he does not have to sanctify them for the night; during the night, he has to sanctify them for the day<sup class="footnote-marker">58</sup><i class="footnote">The night is used to burn the remainder of the previous day’s service; it is an appendix to the day and, since no service is initiated during the night, does not need new preparation.</i>, the words of Rebbi. Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Simeon says, even if he is occupied with service for all of three days, he does not have to sanctify his hands and feet, since staying overnight does not disqualify hands during ancillary services. But to start services it is necessary.”
[Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Joseph explains the <i>baraita:</i> If he sanctified his hands and feet during the day, he does not have to sanctify them for the night; for ancillary services. But to start service he has to sanctify them for the day, the words of Rebbi. Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Simeon says, even if he is occupied with service for all of three days, he does not have to sanctify his hands and feet, since staying overnight does not disqualify hands during ancillary services<sup class="footnote-marker">59</sup><i class="footnote">But if he were unoccupied during the entire night, the next day’s service is a new beginning and needs sanctification of hands.</i>. But to start services it is necessary.]
Rebbi Joḥanan explains the <i>baraita:</i> If he sanctified his hands and feet during the day, he does (not)<sup class="footnote-marker">60</sup><i class="footnote">A word correctly written by the scribe and incorrectly deleted.</i> have to sanctify them for the night; whether to start service or for ancillary services; during the night, he has to sanctify them for the day, the words of Rebbi. Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Simeon says, even if he is occupied with service for all of three days, he does not have to sanctify his hands and feet, since staying overnight does not disqualify hands whether to start service or for ancillary services.
Hilfai said, just as staying overnight does not disqualify hands, so it does not disqualify the basin<sup class="footnote-marker">61</sup><i class="footnote">He disagrees with R. Joḥanan and holds that the water remaining in the basin does not become disqualified at the next dawn.</i>. A <i>baraita</i> disagrees with Rebbi Hilfai. “If he sanctified his hands and feet during the day, he does not have to sanctify them for the night; during the night, he has to sanctify them for the day, the words of Rebbi. Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Simeon says, even if he is occupied with service for all of three days, he does not have to sanctify his hands and feet, since staying overnight does not disqualify hands.” Therefore it disqualifies the basin<sup class="footnote-marker">62</sup><i class="footnote">Since the basin was not mentioned in the statement. Babli <i>Zevaḥim</i> 20a.</i>. The students of Rebbi Joḥanan in the name of Hilfai. So it is: If he sanctified his hands and feet, etc., since staying overnight does not disqualify hands. Therefore it disqualifies the basin, only from day to night<sup class="footnote-marker">63</sup><i class="footnote">Not from night to day since the next day’s service starts with the removal of ashes following R. Joḥanan , and not if the basin was in continuous use during dusk, following R. Ḥiyya bar Joseph.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">64</sup><i class="footnote">One starts with discussing the remainder of Mishnah 1, starting with the meaning of “within 4 cubits”.</i> How, either within four cubits of the ramp or four cubits of the altar? Since we have stated, “It happened that two were equally running up the ramp,” this implies within four cubits of the altar. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, explicitly did Rebbi Ḥiyya state, “he who is first within four cubits of the altar got the right to do it.”
What means הצביעו? Show a finger<sup class="footnote-marker">65</sup><i class="footnote">Since verbs from the root צבע usually meant “to color, to dye”. Cf. Babli 23a.</i>. If one put up one, he is counted; two, he is counted<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">If a Cohen has arthritic fingers and cannot lift a single finger, he may show two which, being close to one another, will be counted as one.</i>; three he is not counted. What means., “is not counted”? Not at all? One does not count the additional. Four, the overseer hits him with a whip and cancels the lottery.
“One does not show a thumb in the Temple,” because of the tricksters<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">Since the thumb is far from the other fingers, the thumb and one other finger might erroneously be counted as two persons.</i>. One does not say from whom<sup class="footnote-marker">66</sup><i class="footnote">The people were not identified by name.</i> in the Temple, but the overseer lifts the cap of one of them and they know that the lottery (proceeds) [starts] from there. Should we not worry, maybe for a friend or a relative<sup class="footnote-marker">67</sup><i class="footnote">That the overseer could predetermine the outcome and therefore the lottery was unfair.</i>? They formed a snail<sup class="footnote-marker">68</sup><i class="footnote">Greek κοχλίας “snail with a spiral shell”. Since the row of Cohanim was “snailing”, the overseer could not determine the exact number of those present. Babli 25a.</i>. How was the lottery proceeding, to the right or to the left? Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, since we did state, the one winning the incense says to the one on his right side, you are with me with the pan<sup class="footnote-marker">69</sup><i class="footnote">On all days other than the Day of Atonement, presenting the incense on the interior altar needed two Cohanim, one carrying the incense and the other carrying hot coals on a pan.</i>, this implies that it proceeded to the right. The students of Rebbi Jonah in the name of Rebbi Hilfai: It is as follows. The lottery proceeds to the left, the winner adds to the right. It is preferable that one should win over whom the lottery passed twice, rather than one over whom the lottery passed only once<sup class="footnote-marker">70</sup><i class="footnote">The previous argument did not prove anything.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">71</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 23a, Tosephta 1:12, Tosephta <i>Ševuot</i> 1:4, <i>Sifry Num.</i> 161.</i> It happened that one preceded another to within four cubits of the altar. The other took the knife and stuck it into his heart. Rebbi Sadoq<sup class="footnote-marker">72</sup><i class="footnote">Since Rabban Joḥanan ben Zakkai asked Vespasian for medical treatment for R. Sadoq, the introduction of the lottery must be dated to the times of direct Roman rule in Judea.</i> stood on the steps of the Hall and said to them, listen to me, my brethren, the House of Israel. It is written, <i>if a corpse be found</i><sup class="footnote-marker">73</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Deut.</i> 21:1.</i><i>.</i> etc. <i>Your elders and your judges shall go out</i><sup class="footnote-marker">74</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Deut.</i> 21:2.</i><i>.</i> From where do we have to measure, from the Temple or from the courtyards? All the people started to cry. While they still were crying, the father of the child<sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote">In the impurity of the dead.</i> came and told them, I am atoning for you. The child is still fluttering, so the knife did not become impure<sup class="footnote-marker">76</sup><i class="footnote">The sheep of the daily morning sacrifice. He is the Cohen with whom the counting of the lottery stops; the following 12 are those lined up to his right.</i>. This teaches that impurity was worse for them than spilling blood, a shame.
Rebbi Joḥanan said, to make a procession<sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote">Latin <i>pompa,</i> Greek πομπή “solemn procession”. One tries to have as many Cohanim as possible involved in order to increase the solemnity.<br>Babli 24b, bottom.</i> on the occasion. Rebbi said, could not the Cohen who was removing the ashes from the interior altar himself clean the candelabra? But to make a procession on the occasion. There, we have stated: “He deposits the flask on the second step and leaves;<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Mishnah Tamid</i> 3:9, speaking of the Cohen who cleans 5 lights of the candelabrum and refills them with oil.</i>” “he takes the flask from the second step and leaves.<sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Mishnah Tamid</i> 6:1; the same Cohen returns, cleans the remaining two lights on the candelabrum, refills, and lights them, when he enters the Sanctuary a second time.</i>” Rebbi Joḥanan said, why does he enter twice for incense? Only to make a procession on the occasion. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, it is a biblical command: <i>in the morning, in the morning, when he cleans the lights he shall burn the incense</i><sup class="footnote-marker">88</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ex.</i> 30:7.</i><i>.</i> What does Rebbi Joḥanan do with this? He could enter to clean and to burn incense<sup class="footnote-marker">89</sup><i class="footnote">The verse does not require different persons for the different jobs (also we already had interpreted <i>in the morning, in the morning</i> as meaning “early in the morning, cf. Note 49.)</i>.

Halakhah 2

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> The second lottery: Who slaughters<sup class="footnote-marker">76</sup><i class="footnote">The sheep of the daily morning sacrifice. He is the Cohen with whom the counting of the lottery stops; the following 12 are those lined up to his right.</i>, who pours<sup class="footnote-marker">77</sup><i class="footnote">The blood of the daily morning sacrifice.</i>, who removes the ashes from the interior altar, who cleans the candelabrum, and who brings the parts to the ramp<sup class="footnote-marker">78</sup><i class="footnote">The parts were first transported to the Western side of lower part of the ramp (Mishnah <i>Šeqalim</i> 8:8); then the Cohanim took a prayer break to recite the <i>Šemaˋ</i>(Mishnah <i>Tamid</i> 4:3, end) and only afterwards were the parts brought to the fire on top of the altar. The way the sheep was cut up is detailed in <i>Tamid</i> 4:2–3.</i>: head and leg<sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote">The head and the right hind leg are carried by the fifth Cohen in line.</i>, the two front legs, spine and leg<sup class="footnote-marker">80</sup><i class="footnote">The left hind leg with tail and kidneys, by the 7th Cohen.</i>, breast and fat<sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote">The breast with the neck and two ribs on each side connected to lung and heart.</i>, two side pieces<sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote">With spine, liver, and spleen, by the 9th Cohen.</i>, and the intestines,<sup class="footnote-marker">83</sup><i class="footnote">Brought in a vessel, with the feet lying on top.</i> and the fine flour<sup class="footnote-marker">84</sup><i class="footnote">The order of carrying, and of distribution to the Cohanim, was not that indicated by the Mishnah but head, breast, front legs, two side pieces, spine and back leg (Note 130). The order of the first and the last four is not in dispute.</i>, and the pan-baked breads<sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote">Latin <i>pompa,</i> Greek πομπή “solemn procession”. One tries to have as many Cohanim as possible involved in order to increase the solemnity.<br>Babli 24b, bottom.</i>, and the wine<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Mishnah Tamid</i> 3:9, speaking of the Cohen who cleans 5 lights of the candelabrum and refills them with oil.</i>. Thirteen Cohanim won here. Ben Azzai said before Rebbi Aqiba in the name of Rebbi Joshua, it was brought in the way of its walking<sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Mishnah Tamid</i> 6:1; the same Cohen returns, cleans the remaining two lights on the candelabrum, refills, and lights them, when he enters the Sanctuary a second time.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> From where the cleaning of the interior altar<sup class="footnote-marker">90</sup><i class="footnote">Since in contrast to the exterior altar, removing ashes from the interior incense altar is never mentioned in the Torah.</i>? Rebbi Pedat in the name of Rebbi Eleazar: <i>He shall throw it next to the altar, to the East, on the place of ashes</i><sup class="footnote-marker">91</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 1:16, referring to the crop of a pigeon brought as elevation offering. Cf. <i>Sifra Wayyiqra</i>1<i>Pereq</i> 9(3).</i><i>.</i> It is unnecessary<sup class="footnote-marker">92</sup><i class="footnote">The mention <i>on the place of ashes</i> is not needed to fix the place; it instructs the Cohen where to put the ashes. Babli <i>Meˋilah</i> 12a.</i>. If to designate [the place], it already is written, <i>next to the altar.</i> If to teach you that it should be put to the East of the ramp, it already is written, <i>to the East.</i> Also he explained, <i>next to the altar, next to the altar</i><sup class="footnote-marker">93</sup><i class="footnote">The first quote is from <i>Lev.</i> 1:16, the second <i>Lev.</i> 6:3, about the ashes from the exterior altar formally deposited next to the altar. Since this case is explicit the exterior altar, the other is taken implicitly to refer to the interior altar.</i><i>.</i> Since in one case it is to the East of the ramp, so in the other case it is to the East of the ramp. From where that it is forbidden for usufruct<sup class="footnote-marker">94</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Meˋilah</i> 3:4 states that from the ashes from the interior altar and the candelabrum one may not have usufruct but taking them is not larceny.</i>? Rebbi La in the name of Rebbi Eleazar: <i>to a pure place</i><sup class="footnote-marker">95</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 6:4. The quote is inappropriate since the verse speaks of the remainder of the ashes on the exterior altar which are transported to a pure place outside the sacred precinct.</i><i>,</i> that its place shall be pure<sup class="footnote-marker">96</sup><i class="footnote">It seems that here “pure” is taken in the sense of “untouched”.</i>. Rebbi Zeˋira in the name of Rebbi Eleazar did not say so but, from where that the cleaning of the exterior altar is forbidden for usufruct? The verse says, <i>to the place of ashes,</i> that it be its place forever. From where the cleaning of the interior altar? <i>He shall sprinkle on it</i><sup class="footnote-marker">91</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 1:16, referring to the crop of a pigeon brought as elevation offering. Cf. <i>Sifra Wayyiqra</i>1<i>Pereq</i> 9(3).</i><i>, he shall burn incense</i><sup class="footnote-marker">98</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ex.</i> 30:7. The quote is incomplete since the argument is a comparison of <i>he shall sprinkle on it,</i> and <i>he shall burn incense on it.</i></i><i>.</i> Since sprinkling is on its body<sup class="footnote-marker">99</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in Halakhah 5:7, the High Priest on the Day of Atonement is commanded to sprinkle blood on the interior altar <i>on it,</i> on the cleaned metal surface directly, not on ashes or unburned incense. The rule is then transferred to everyday’s burning of incense since the same expression is used.</i>, also burning incense on its body. From where that the interior altar is forbidden for usufruct? An argument <i>de minore ad majus.</i> If from the exterior altar it is forbidden, so much more from the interior<sup class="footnote-marker">100</sup><i class="footnote">Since the external altar is accessible to all Cohanim at all times, the internal only to a selected Cohen twice a day.</i>.
Rebbi Zeˋira in the name of Rebbi Ḥanina: Incense which was extinguished becomes defective even in carats<sup class="footnote-marker">101</sup><i class="footnote">Even if entire grains of incense are not touched by the fire, they become disqualified. Babli <i>Menaḥot</i>24b.</i>; for consumption is written only for the external altar<sup class="footnote-marker">102</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i>6:3</i>. A wick which was extinguished needs replacement<sup class="footnote-marker">103</sup><i class="footnote">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i>88b.</i>. Immediately? The students of Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Julianus say, first it needs to be cooled. Does the oil have to be replaced? The word of Rebbi Samuel bar Rav Isaac implies that oil has to be replaced. Rebbi Samuel bar Rav Isaac asked, now on the winter solstice half a <i>log</i> for each light, on the summer solstice half a log for each light<sup class="footnote-marker">104</sup><i class="footnote">Since the candelabrum has to be lit “from evening to morning’ (<i>Ex.</i>27:21), one would assume that filling the same volume of oil in winter and summer means that in the summer the remnants of the previous night’s oil have to be discarded. Cf. Babli 15a.</i>? Rebbi Yose said, from this you cannot conclude anything, as we have stated there<sup class="footnote-marker">105</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Šeqalim</i> 5:1.</i>, “Ben Bevay for the skeins”, he was threading the wicks<sup class="footnote-marker">106</sup><i class="footnote">If larger wicks are used in summer than in winter, the same amount of oil can be burned in all seasons. The Babli presumes without discussion that the oil has to be replaced, <i>Menaḥot</i>88b.</i>.
Here, you are saying, he cleans and then he burns the incense; but there, you are saying, he burns the incense and then he cleans<sup class="footnote-marker">107</sup><i class="footnote">In Mishnah 1:2 it is stated that the High Priest first burns the incense and then cleans the lights; it is presumed that this was the order during the entire year when ordinary priests were serving. But in Mishnah 2:3 the cleaning of the candelabrum is part of the first lottery, while buring the incense is mentioned only in Mishnah 2:4 (confirmed by Mishnah <i>Tamid</i> 5:2). The Mishnaiot are inconsistent with another.</i>. Rebbi Joḥanan said, this is <i>Tamid</i> of Rebbi Simeon from Mitzpeh<sup class="footnote-marker">108</sup><i class="footnote">Chapter 2 follows the Mishnah in <i>Tamid</i>, which follows the teachings of Rebbi Simeon from Mitzpeh. Tosephta 1:13.</i>. Rebbi Aḥa bar Jacob said, but not all of it; there are sayings questioned by the rabbis<sup class="footnote-marker">109</sup><i class="footnote">Tractate <i>Tamid</i> is mostly but not totally, based on the teachings of Rebbi Simeon from Mitzpeh.</i>. Rebbi Ḥizqiah, Rebbi Aḥa, in the name of Rebbi Abbahu: It is <i>Middot</i> of Rebbi Eliezer ben Jacob<sup class="footnote-marker">110</sup><i class="footnote">The parts in <i>Tamid</i> inconsistent with the teachings of Rebbi Simeon from Mitzpeh are attributed to R. Eliezer ben Jacob I who is the source of most of Mishnah <i>Middot</i> (Babli 16a).</i>. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, but not all of it; there are sayings questioned by the rabbis. What is the reason of Rebbi Simeon from Mitzpeh? <i>In the morning, in the morning, when he cleans the lights he shall burn the incense on it</i><sup class="footnote-marker">111</sup><i class="footnote"><i>. Ex.</i> 30:7 clearly mentions cleaning the lights before burning the incense.</i><i>.</i> Rebbi Aḥa, Rebbi Ḥinena in the name of Rebbi Simeon ben Rebbi: The reason of the rabbis, <i>outside the curtain of the testimonial in the Tent of Meeting, Aaron and his sons shall arrange it from evening to morning</i><sup class="footnote-marker">112</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ex.</i> 27:21 (badly misquoted). If the burning of incense in the evening were after lighting the candelabrum, the lighting would not be the last action in the Sanctuary before the next morning.</i><i>;</i> that there shall be only the cleaning of the lights<sup class="footnote-marker">113</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 26a.</i>.
Rebbi Joḥanan said, they did not institute a lottery for the evening but said, he who won in the morning shall have won in the evening<sup class="footnote-marker">113</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 26a.</i>. But was it not stated: Just as the lottery is in the morning, so it is in the evening? The winner won for himself. Rebbi Ḥizqiah in the name of Rebbi Abun bar Cahana: Explain it that it was on the Sabbath; one for the entering watch, the other for the leaving watch<sup class="footnote-marker">114</sup><i class="footnote">Since a new watch, another family of Cohanim, took over the service after the morning sacrifices, it is obvious that the Cohen who won in the morning is no longer present at the Temple in the afternoon.</i>.
Rebbi Joḥanan said, they did not decide about the two logs in the morning<sup class="footnote-marker">115</sup><i class="footnote">There was no lottery to determine who brought the obligatory two logs to the altar in the morning, but the Cohen chosen to remove the ashes had to bring the new logs and set up an orderly fireplace on the altar.</i>. Rebbi Yose said, a <i>baratta</i> says so, every day (a he-goat)<sup class="footnote-marker">116</sup><i class="footnote">This word is a misquote from Mishnah 6 which is not quoted here since one refers to Mishnah 5 about the daily sacrifice, which was a sheep.</i> is brought by eleven, and it does not mention anything in the morning. Rebbi Shammai asked, why did they not decide about the two logs in the morning? Rebbi Mana said, did Rebbi Shammai not hear that Rebbi Joḥanan said, they did not decide about the two logs in the morning; and Rebbi Yose said, a <i>baraita</i> says so? He turned around and said, yes, he had heard. But he is a person who heard a statement and questions it: Why did they decide about two logs in the evening and did not decide about two logs in the morning<sup class="footnote-marker">117</sup><i class="footnote">Tosaphot <i>Menaḥot</i>89b–90a, s. v. תמיד point out that the bringing of logs to the altar in the morning belongs to the preparation, covered by the first lottery. Only in the afternoon was the bringing of two logs part of the service of the daily sacrifice. Since the early morning preparation was in the night, there was no need to increase the number of participants for <i>pompa.</i></i>?
“Thirteen won here.” And it was stated on this<sup class="footnote-marker">118</sup><i class="footnote">Tosephta 1:13.</i>: “Sometimes fourteen, sometimes fifteen, sometimes sixteen, no less and no more.” Normally by nine<sup class="footnote-marker">119</sup><i class="footnote">Plus the four who precede the presentation of the daily sacrifice makes 13.</i>, and on Tabernacles in the hand of one a vial of water, these are ten<sup class="footnote-marker">120</sup><i class="footnote">Together 14.</i>. In the evening by eleven; in the hands of two, two wooden logs. On the Sabbath by eleven, itself by nine, two, in their hands two cups of incense of the shew-bread; this makes (fifteen) [fourteen]<sup class="footnote-marker">121</sup><i class="footnote">Both in the evening of every day and in the morning of the Sabbath. The corrector’s text clearly is in error.</i>. On the Sabbath of Tabernacles, in the hand of one a vial of water, this makes sixteen.
<i>He shall bring</i> <i>it</i><sup class="footnote-marker">122</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 6:7, on the presentation of the High-Priest’s pan-baked breads. Cf.i 34a</i>, before the additional sacrifices, but when he repeats <i>you shall sacrifice</i> even after the libations<sup class="footnote-marker">123</sup><i class="footnote">The libations of wine belonging to the daily sacrifice, preceding the additional sacrifices of special days.</i>. There are Tannaim who state, before the libations. He who says before the libations, before the wine libations. He who says after the libations, after the libations of fine flour. <sup class="footnote-marker">124</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 34a.</i> The fine flour precedes the pan-baked breads; even though this is for the fire and that is for the fire, this is a private sacrifice<sup class="footnote-marker">125</sup><i class="footnote">The High Priest’s private offering, although part of the public ceremony.</i> and the other a public sacrifice. The pan-baked bread precede the cups<sup class="footnote-marker">126</sup><i class="footnote">On the Sabbath, containing the incense which accompanied the shew-bread on the table in the Sanctuary.</i>; even though this is a private sacrifice and the other a public sacrifice, this is frequent but the other is not frequent<sup class="footnote-marker">127</sup><i class="footnote">The wine libations accompanying the sacrifices were poured into bowls with small holes on the bottom through which the wine flowed onto the altar in sufficiently small amounts so that the wine evaporated and did not extinguish the flame.</i>. The pan-baked breads precede the wine since this is for the fire but that is for the bowls<sup class="footnote-marker">127</sup><i class="footnote">The wine libations accompanying the sacrifices were poured into bowls with small holes on the bottom through which the wine flowed onto the altar in sufficiently small amounts so that the wine evaporated and did not extinguish the flame.</i>. Cups and wine, which one has precedence? Is that not the Mishnah, incense before the wine<sup class="footnote-marker">128</sup><i class="footnote">Since in Mishnah 3 wine is mentioned last, and on the Sabbath one mentions the two cups containing incense with the daily sacrifice, it should be clear that incense precedes the wine.</i>? Here for a private offering<sup class="footnote-marker">129</sup><i class="footnote">The only open question is how to handle incense and wine brought with a private offering.</i>, there for public offering.
So is the Mishnah<sup class="footnote-marker">130</sup><i class="footnote">The missing part of the Mishnah, the list according to Ben Azzai. Babli 25b.</i>: head and leg<sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote">The head and the right hind leg are carried by the fifth Cohen in line.</i>, breast and fat<sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote">The breast with the neck and two ribs on each side connected to lung and heart.</i>, the front legs, two side pieces<sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote">With spine, liver, and spleen, by the 9th Cohen.</i>, spine and leg<sup class="footnote-marker">80</sup><i class="footnote">The left hind leg with tail and kidneys, by the 7th Cohen.</i>. Rebbi Joḥanan said, the reason of Ben Azzai: <i>you shall burn the entire he-goat on the altar</i><sup class="footnote-marker">131</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ex.</i> 29:18. walking.</i>, it should look as if it went walking onto the altar. Head and leg, and you are saying so? Rebbi Mana said, if it stretches out its head<sup class="footnote-marker">132</sup><i class="footnote">In order to start walking.</i> it lifts the foot.

Halakhah 3

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> The third lottery, newcomers for incense come and participate in the lottery. The fourth, newcomers and old-timers, who brings the limbs from the ramp to the altar?
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rebbi Ḥanina said, nobody ever participated in the lottery and repeated<sup class="footnote-marker">133</sup><i class="footnote">It means that nobody ever won in that lottery and repeated. Babli 26a, where R. Ḥanina says that bringing the incense makes people rich.</i>. Rebbi Yose said, the Mishnah says so, “newcomers for incense come and participate in the lottery.” Rebbi Ḥanina said, the same is true for the pan<sup class="footnote-marker">69</sup><i class="footnote">On all days other than the Day of Atonement, presenting the incense on the interior altar needed two Cohanim, one carrying the incense and the other carrying hot coals on a pan.</i>. Rebbi Yose said, a <i>baraita</i> says so, “the one winning the incense says to the one on his right side, you are with me with the pan,” You have to say that two Cohanim are blessed every time<sup class="footnote-marker">134</sup><i class="footnote">Since obviously the man standing next to the winner also never won before.</i>. Rav said, <i>May the Eternal bless his might and may You desire the action of his hands</i><sup class="footnote-marker">135</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Deut.</i> 33:11, the blessing of Moses. The Babli interprets חַיִל as “riches”, whereas the Yerushalmi reads it as “physical power”.</i><i>.</i> It happened that a man whose arm atrophied<sup class="footnote-marker">136</sup><i class="footnote">The arm could not really have atrophied since that would have disqualified the Cohen from serving; it must have been a case of weakness in the arm which was healed by his serving with the incense.</i> but he did not refrain from it, to uphold what had been said, <i>may the Eternal bless his might and may You desire the action of his hands.</i>

Halakhah 4

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> The daily sacrifice is brought by nine persons, by ten, by eleven, by twelve, neither less nor more. How is this? Itself by nine<sup class="footnote-marker">119</sup><i class="footnote">Plus the four who precede the presentation of the daily sacrifice makes 13.</i>, and on Tabernacles in the hand of one a vial of water, these are ten<sup class="footnote-marker">120</sup><i class="footnote">Together 14.</i>. In the evening by eleven; itself by nine and in the hands of two, two wooden logs. On the Sabbath by eleven, itself by nine, two, in their hands two cups of incense of the shew-bread;.. On the Sabbath of Tabernacles, in the hand of one a vial of water.<br>A he-goat is brought by eleven, the meat by five, the intestines, and the fine flour, and the wine, each by two.<br>A bull is brought by twenty-four, head and leg<sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote">The head and the right hind leg are carried by the fifth Cohen in line.</i>, the head by one and the leg by two; spine and leg<sup class="footnote-marker">80</sup><i class="footnote">The left hind leg with tail and kidneys, by the 7th Cohen.</i>, the spine by two and the leg by two; breast and fat<sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote">The breast with the neck and two ribs on each side connected to lung and heart.</i>, the breast by one and the fat by three; the two front legs by two; the two side pieces<sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote">With spine, liver, and spleen, by the 9th Cohen.</i> by two; the intestines, and the fine flour<sup class="footnote-marker">149</sup><i class="footnote">Which is 3/10 of an <i>epha</i> or about 3.6 liter of flour mixed with ½ <i>hin</i> of oil, about 3.5 liter.</i>, and the wine<sup class="footnote-marker">150</sup><i class="footnote">Also half a <i>hin,</i></i> by three each. When has this been said? For a public offering. But for a private offering, if one wants to sacrifice, he sacrifices<sup class="footnote-marker">151</sup><i class="footnote">If a single Cohen wants to do all the carrying, he may do it.</i>. Skinning and cutting into pieces is the same for these and for those<sup class="footnote-marker">152</sup><i class="footnote">It need not be done by Cohanim.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <i>They shall arrange</i><sup class="footnote-marker">137</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 1:7. The theme of the Halakhah is to find a biblical source for the number of Cohanim used to bring the parts of the daily sacrifices to the altar.</i><i>.</i> I could think, a hundred; I could think, a thousand. <sup class="footnote-marker">138</sup><i class="footnote">The remainder of the Paragraph also is <i>Sifra MesoraˋParashah</i> 5(5–9). Its topic is the interpretation of prescriptive biblical verses in the absence of numerical data. The theory expounded here is what the author has called the axiom of definiteness: Biblical language in legal contexts is definite (H. Guggenheimer, <i>Logical Problems in Jewish Tradition,</i> in: Confrontations with Judaism, Ph. Longworth ed., London 1966., pp. 171–196, in particular pp. 174–175.) In the situation considered here it is noted that the set of numbers &gt;1 has a smallest element, 2, but no largest one. Therefore an indefinite plural used in a biblical law must mean 2, otherwise the meaning would not be definite. This is applied to the laws of <i>zava,</i> a woman impure by non-menstrual blood flow for <i>many days.</i> By the principle of definiteness this means that days are 2, the number of <i>many days</i> is the smallest number &gt;2, or 3.</i> Rebbi Aqiba said, anywhere you could understand many or you could understand few, if you took the many you took nothing, if you took few you took<sup class="footnote-marker">139</sup><i class="footnote">Babli <i>Megillah</i> 17a, <i>Sanhedrin</i> 5a.</i>. It was stated: Rebbi Jehudah ben Bathyra said, two measures; one finite, the other infinite. Everybody measures with the finite measure, but nobody measures with the infinite measure. Rebbi Nehemiah said, does the verse come to open or to lock in? It does not come to lock in but to open<sup class="footnote-marker">140</sup><i class="footnote">In Babylonian sources, this statement is credited to R. Yose; <i>Seder Olam</i> Chapter 1 (in the author’s edition, Northvale 1998, p. 3, Note 5, pp. 5–8.)</i>. If you are saying <i>days</i><sup class="footnote-marker">141</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 15:25.</i> are ten, they could be 100 or 200 or 1’000 or 10’000. But if you say <i>days</i> are two, you did unlock. Rebbi Muna<sup class="footnote-marker">142</sup><i class="footnote">The Tanna.</i> said in the name of Rebbi Jehudah. <i>Days</i> are two. I could think that <i>days</i> are many. If they are many, why is it said, <i>many?</i> Therefore the verse only spoke of few days. How much are they? It means two; <i>many</i> are three. I could think that <i>many (days)</i> means ten. It says <i>days</i> and it says <i>many.</i> Since the minimum of <i>days</i> are two, so for <i>many,</i> the minimum of many are three. I could think that two and three make five. But is it said, <i>days [and many]?</i> It only is said, <i>many days.</i> How is this? These <i>many</i> should be more than two. How many are they? It implies three.
<sup class="footnote-marker">143</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph is <i>Sifra Wayyiqra I Pereq</i> 6(1).</i><i>The sons of Aaron shall arrange</i><sup class="footnote-marker">137</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 1:7. The theme of the Halakhah is to find a biblical source for the number of Cohanim used to bring the parts of the daily sacrifices to the altar.</i><i>.</i> I could think, a hundred; the verse says, <i>the Cohen shall arrange</i><sup class="footnote-marker">144</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 1:12.</i><i>.</i> [If <i>the Cohen shall arrange</i>,] I could think that a single Cohen should arrange all the limbs; the verse says, <i>they shall arrange.</i> How is this? One Cohen arranges two limbs. How many limbs are there? Ten, and one for the intestines. It turns out that the lamb comes up by six (priests}, the words of Rebbi Ismael. Rebbi Aqiba says, <i>they shall arrange,</i> two; <i>the sons of Aaron,</i> two; <i>the priests,</i> two<sup class="footnote-marker">145</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 27a.</i>. This teaches that the lamb comes up by six {priests}. [<i>The priest,</i> to include the bald-headed, the words of Rebbi Jehudah.]<sup class="footnote-marker">146</sup><i class="footnote">The sentence in brackets was added by the corrector, probably from <i>Sifra.</i> It has no connection with the topic under discussion. Babli <i>Bekhorot</i> 43b.</i>
But does the verse not speak of cattle<sup class="footnote-marker">146</sup><i class="footnote">The sentence in brackets was added by the corrector, probably from <i>Sifra.</i> It has no connection with the topic under discussion. Babli <i>Bekhorot</i> 43b.</i>? Where does the verse imply that it is written about the daily morning sacrifice? Simeon bar Abba, Rebbi Joḥanan in the name of Rebbi Yannai: It is written here<sup class="footnote-marker">147</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 1:7 is written in the paragraph about elevation offerings of cattle; only <i>Lev.</i>1:12 is about elevation offerings of sheep, including the daily sacrifice. The argument of the preceding paragraph seems pointless.</i> arranging, and it is written there, <i>the Cohen shall arrange them.</i> Since concerning the arrangement mentioned there, the verse speaks about the daily morning sacrifice, so also concerning the arrangement mentioned here, the verse speaks about the daily morning sacrifice. Ulla bar Ismael in the name of Rebbi Eleazar, this is unnecessary. From the meaning of <i>they shall arrange,</i> do we not understand that they are two? And you explain, <i>they shall arrange,</i> two; <i>the sons of Aaron,</i> two; <i>the priests,</i> two; and it was stated so: Nothing precedes the daily sacrifice but incense<sup class="footnote-marker">49,</sup><i class="footnote">Since the daily sacrifice is scheduled בבוקר “in the morning (<i>Ex.</i> 29:39) but the incense בבוקר בבוקר “in the early morning (<i>Ex.</i> 30:7); cf. Halakhah 3:5. Babli <i>Pesaḥim</i>59a.</i><sup class="footnote-marker">148</sup><i class="footnote">Ulla's argument goes as follows. Since arranging the wood on the altar belongs to the preparations of the morning service, and no cattle can be offered as elevation offering (or any other) before the daily morning sacrifice, necessarily Lev. 1:7 is written for the preparation of all offerings for the new day, including the daily sacrifice.</i>.
Three could bring it up; why is a he-goat brought by eleven? Only to make a procession.
The rabbis of Caesarea say, why is a bull brought by 24? To make a procession on the occasion, under the heading, <i>in God’s House</i> we <i>shall walk in excitement</i><sup class="footnote-marker">153</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ps.</i> 55:15.</i><i>.</i> Since one explains, <i>they shall arrange,</i> two; <i>the sons of Aaron,</i> two; <i>the priests,</i> two; from here that a private person’s bull should be brought by six<sup class="footnote-marker">154</sup><i class="footnote">Since <i>Lev.</i> 1:7, to which this explanation refers, is written in the paragraph about private elevation offerings of cattle.</i>.

Chapter 3



Halakhah 1

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> The overseer said to them<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Every day of the year, when the daily morning sacrifice was brought at dawn.</i>, “go and see whether the time of slaughter has arrived.” When it arrived, the lookout says “it is radiant.” Mathatias ben Samuel<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">He is mentioned in Mishnah <i>Šeqalim</i>5:1 as overseer of the lotteries. The sources are not unanimous about the meaning of these names, whether they came with the job or are a remembrance of outstanding personalities who once filled these positions. Some moderns presume that the list is of the last officials serving in the Second Temple.</i> says, “was the entire East illuminated up to what is in Hebron<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Even though Hebron is South of Jerusalem, as explained at the end of the Halakhah.</i>?” And he<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">The lookout.</i> answers “yes”.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">The Halakhah is copied in <i>Roš Haššanah</i>2:1 (<b>א</b>).</i>“The overseer said to them,” etc. What means <i>borqi? Bareqet</i><sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">The word denotes one of the precious stones in the breast plate of the High Priest, usually identified as agate or emerald. The word means radiant, from בָּרָק “lightning”.</i><i>.</i> There<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">In Babylonia; in the formulation of the Babli 28b בָּרָק בַּרְקַאי.</i>, they are saying, בְּרוֹק בּוֹרְקָה, getting light, radiant.
May one witness be believed<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">The Babli holds in general that a single witness can be believed in matters of prohibitions; the biblical requirement of two witnesses is binding only in criminal cases and matters that may have implications in criminal law. From the present paragraph it seems that the Yerushalmi does not accept this in general but that in cases where one witness is sufficient there is no difference between male or female witnesses.</i>? It is different here since one cannot control him; should we not worry and say, by the time somebody climbs up and goes out it will shine<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">While the time indicated must be approximately correct, since one asks only at the end of the night, and by the time somebody climbs up to check it clearly will be dawn, this does not prove that at the time of the assertion dawn was really visible. The text cannot be amended and the “not” deleted since it is confirmed by both sources.</i>? The matter can be verified. If one witness says, this male was born on the Sabbath, one circumcises him on his word<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">Even though circumcising on the Sabbath a child not born on the Sabbath is a deadly sin.</i>. Rebbi Immi was carrying on the result of elapsed time<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">Arabic ملوهَ “interval of time”. He computed the end of the Sabbath astronomically, for a smooth terrestrial globe; a severe restriction for Tiberias situated on a steep Eastern slope.</i>. Rebbi Mattaniah was carrying on the saying of the moon shining<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">The translation of איביריתא is conjectural. The direction of the shining part of the moon indicates the position of the sun, from which its position below the horizon (of a smooth terrestrial globe) can be inferred without complicated computations.</i>. Rebbi Immi was (carrying) [circumcising]<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">The text in parenthesis is from <i>Yoma,</i> the one in braces from <i>Roš Haššanah.</i> Since Hippos was on the Eastern shore of the Lake of Galilee, so that for people in Tiberias on the Western shore the sun shone over Hippos in the morning, the statement cannot refer to the Sabbath. The reading of <i>Roš Haššanah</i> has to be accepted. Since circumcision has to be performed during daytime, R. Immi is consistently restrictive; in this case he does not rely on astronomical computations of sunrise but on the much later observation of the sun appearing over the mountains to the East.</i> on the saying of women, the sun was over Hippos.
And why “up to who is in Hebron? And he answers yes”? He comes to commemorate the merit of the Patriarchs.

Halakhah 2

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Why did they need this? Because once the moon shone<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">As the Halakhah points out, this can happen only in the second half of a month and therefore could not refer to a Day of Atonement.</i> and they thought that it dawned to the East; they slaughtered the daily sacrifice and had to bring it outside to the place of burning<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">The outside place reserved for the burning of disqualified sacrifices or those whose blood was brought into the Sanctuary and which could not be burned on the altar.</i>. Then they brought the Cohen<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">All Babli and independent Mishnah texts read: The High Priest.</i> to the place of immersion. This was the rule in the Temple: Everybody who spread his legs<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">Defecated. A biblical expression <i>Jud.</i>3:26.</i> needed immersion<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">Of his entire body in a <i>miqweh.</i></i>; and everybody who urinated needed sanctification of hands and feet<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">From the basin in the courtyard.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Moonlight comes up as a beam; sunlight spreads over the entire East<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">The reason given in the Mishnah is difficult to accept. In the Babli 28b it is explained that it was a cloudy day where the moonlight also was diffuse.</i>. So far if it was the end of the month; if it was the start<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">Even if one accepts the explanation of the Mishnah, the inquiry would only be necessary towards the end of the month when the moon rises towards morning.</i>?
<sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote">A somewhat garbled version of a text in <i>Berakhot</i> 1:1 (Notes 63–70) and <i>Gen. rabba</i> 50(15).</i> Rebbi Ḥanina said: From the appearance of the “morning hind”<sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote">The zodiacal light.</i> until the first rays of light in the East a man can walk four mil<sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote">Since a person is presumed to be able to walk 40 <i>mil</i> on a full day at the equinoxes, this comes to 72 min.</i>. From the first rays of light in the East until sunrise a man can walk four mil<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote">Babli <i>Pesaḥim</i> 94a,</i>. From where do we know that from the appearance of “the morning hind” until the first rays of light on the East there are four mil? [since it is written]<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Gen.</i> 19:15.</i>: <i>and when the morning came, the angels urged Lot, saying</i><sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote">It is clear that the argument is not relevant to the question asked here, but to the time elapsing between first dawn and sunrise. To complete the proof, one has to add a reference to v. 23, found in <i>Berakhot</i> and <i>Gen. rabba,</i> which states that Lot arrived in Zoar at the time of sunrise.</i><i>.</i> From Sodom to Zoar there are four mil. It is farther than that<sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote">In the Babli, <i>Pesaḥim</i> 93b, R. Ḥanina is quoted that he checked out the distance and it was 5 <i>mil.</i></i>. Rebbi Zeˋira said: the angel was flattening the road before them. And from where that from the first rays of light in the East until sunrise there are four mil? When, <i>and when,</i> one thing compares to another<sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote">The additional <i>and</i> permits to compare the one time specified in Scripture to the other, the time between visibility of the zodiacal light and first dawn. </i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote">This and the following paragraph also are from <i>Berakhot.</i></i>Rebbi Yose bar Abun said: Anybody who identifies the “morning hind” with the planet Venus is in error; that planet sometimes is too early and sometimes too late<sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote">Sometimes Venus sets still during the night and sometimes it still is seen after sunrise.</i>. What is it? It is like two double horns of light that arise from the East and illuminate.
<sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph was added to the ms. by a corrector. While there is no logical necessity for the addition of this text, it is copied from a <i>Yoma</i> text, not from <i>Berakhot.</i> In <i>Berakhot</i> the quotes from <i>Esther</i> make sense, v. 6:11 preceding 6:12. The paragraph also is copied in <i>Qonteros Aḥaron</i>(Q, Chapter 1, Note 44; p. 311) which also quotes 6:12 before v 6:11. The text of Q is identical with that given here except that the Aramaic endings are ה not א; babylonized spelling is to be expected from all correctors.</i>[Explanation<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">Greek δήλωμα.</i>: The great Rebbi Ḥiyya and Rebbi Simeon ben Halaphta were walking in the valley of Arbela before morning and saw “the morning hind” that started radiating. The great Rebbi Ḥiyya said to Rebbi Simeon ben Halaphta: Great man, so will be the deliverance of Israel; it starts out very small and grows and radiates as it goes on. What is the reason <sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Micha</i> 7:8.</i><i>When he</i><sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote">In the biblical text: I.</i><i>shall dwell in darkness, the Eternal is my light.</i> So also at the start <sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Esth.</i> 2:21.</i><i>Mordocai was sitting at the king’s gate.”</i> After that <sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Esth.</i>6:12.</i><i>Mordocai returned to the king’s gate.</i> After that <sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Esth.</i>6:11.</i><i>Haman took the garment and the horse.</i> After that: <sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Esth.</i> 8:15.</i><i>Mordocai left the king’s presence in royal garb.</i> After that: <sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Esth.</i> 8:16.</i><i>The Jews had light and joy.</i>]
It was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote">Tosephta 1:16, Babli <i>Zevaḥim</i> 20b, Yerushalmi <i>Kilaim</i> 9:2 Notes 47–48.</i>: “A Cohen who left to speak with another person, if to go a distance, he needs immersion<sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote">As requited by Mishnah 3.</i>; if for a short time he needs sanctification of hands and legs<sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">Since when he returns he starts his service anew; cf. Chapter 2 Note 51.</i>. But is defecation not for a short time? There is a difference for defecation since they treat it as if going a distance.
It was stated: A person sleeping needs immersion, being drowsy needs sanctification of hands and legs. Does a person sleeping need immersion? Did not Rebbi Ḥiyya state<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 25a,69b; <i>Sotah</i> 40b,41b; <i>Qiddušin</i> 78b; <i>Sanhedrin</i> 101b; <i>Tamid</i> 27b. Yerushalmi <i>Pesaḥim</i> 5:12 (Note 247), <i>Sotah</i>7:7 (Note 219).</i>, “there was no sitting in the Temple courtyard except for the kings of the Davidic dynasty;” and Rebbi Immi said in the name of Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish, even for the kings of the Davidic dynasty there was no sitting in the Temple courtyard. Explain it that somebody was supporting himself on a wall and sleeping. But is it not written<sup class="footnote-marker">46</sup><i class="footnote"><i>2S</i>. 7:18.</i>, <i>King David came and sat before the Eternal?</i> Rebbi Ayvo bar Naggari said, he concentrated in prayer<sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote">As required by Mishnah 3.</i>.

Halakhah 3

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Nobody enters the courtyard to serve, even if he was pure, unless he immerses himself. Five immersions and ten sanctifications did the High Priest immerse himself and sanctify on that day, and all of them in the Sanctuary in the Parwa house<sup class="footnote-marker">48</sup><i class="footnote">A subterranean cave inside the walls enclosing the sacred domain. The Babli declares “Parwa” to be the name of a magus or sorcerer.</i>, except this one alone<sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote">Since the Mishnah states that nobody can enter the sacred domain for service unless he immersed himself in water outside the sacred domain, it is obvious that before serving the High Priest also must immerse himself in a <i>miqweh</i> on the Temple Mount but outside the sacred domain</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> So is the Mishnah: No person did enter the courtyard or for service<sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote">Nobody, Cohen or lay person, could enter the sacred domain without ablution. But the Cohen who entered not for service could not start to serve until he underwent a second immersion.</i>, [even if he was pure,] unless he immerses himself. Not only for service but also not for service.
They asked Ben Zoma, where does this immersion come from<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote">Which does not seem to be biblical.</i>? He said to them, since when he enters the holy from the holy he needs immersion<sup class="footnote-marker">52</sup><i class="footnote">As stated later in the Mishnah, if the High Priest changes from his 8 garments used for service outside to white garments used inside the Sanctuary he both immerses himself and sanctifies hands and legs.</i>, from profane to holy so much more? It is not necessary, but from holy to holy he should not need immersion<sup class="footnote-marker">53</sup><i class="footnote">Since he already immersed himself at the start of the service.</i>, from profane to holy he should need immersion<sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">This would be an answer to the question asked at the start of the paragraph, but it is contradicted by the later Mishnaiot.</i>. Rebbi Shammai said, it is the following.
