Rebbi Joḥanan said, he establishes even by word of mouth<sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote">For him the drawing of lots is not indispensable; Babli 39b.</i>. They thought to say, even one today and one tomorrow<sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote">Since the entire service is restricted to one day, this can only mean that for R. Joḥanan it is possible to predetermine the he-goat which is to be the purification sacrifice.</i>. In the opinion of Rebbi Joḥanan who said, even one today and one tomorrow, it is understandable. In the opinion of Rebbi Yannai, why does it say, <i>lots</i><sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote">These sentences have to be switched. For R. Yannai, for whom drawing of lots is indispensable, the lots have to be mentioned. But for R. Joḥanan , for whom the fate of the he-goats can be predetermined, why are lots mentioned at all?</i>? As meritorious deed. A <i>baraita</i> disagrees with Rebbi Joḥanan : The lot makes it a purification sacrifice, giving it the name does not make it a purification sacrifice. He explains it, if the drawing succeeds<sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote">The position of R. Joḥanan is modified. He will agree that using an urn in the service is required. In the case that the High Priest loses the lots which he is lifting, the ceremony does not have to be repeated, the he-goats do not become disqualified, and he can proceed to select the he-goat to be sacrificed following the rules spelled out earlier.</i>. A <i>baraita</i> disagrees with Rebbi Yannai: If he did not draw lots and did not confess it is qualified, only he missed a meritorious deed<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote">Since the objection cannot be answered, practice has to follow R. Joḥanan . Babli 40a.</i>.
<i>For the Eternal</i><sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev</i>. 22:26.</i>, to include the he-goat which is sent away that it can be disqualified for lacking time<sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote">A he-goat which is not at least eight days old may not be used on the Day of Atonement. Even though the he-goat sent into the wilderness is not a sacrifice, by the process of drawing lots it is a potential sacrifice and has to be qualified as such. Babli 63b, <i>Sifra Emor Parasha</i> 8(6).</i>. This comes following what Rebbi Joḥanan said, he establishes even by word of mouth<sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">Since for him it might be the choice of the High Priest to select the he-goat as sacrifice, one understands that a separate verse is needed to require both he-goats to be eligible at the same time. But for R. Yannai, for whom only the drawing determines which animal is chosen, it should be obvious that both have to be eligible. Then why is a separate verse needed?</i>. They thought to say, even one today and one tomorrow. In the opinion of Rebbi Joḥanan who said, even one today and one tomorrow, it is understandable. In the opinion of Rebbi Yannai, why is there said, <i>lots</i>? Should we not be concerned that maybe it is drawn for the Eternal? He explains it if he wants to draw lots<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote">To prohibit that one could take the risk that an ineligible animal be drawn as sacrifice and in this case start again with another pair and a new drawing.</i>.
If one slaughtered outside<sup class="footnote-marker">46</sup><i class="footnote">Outside the Temple domain, which is a deadly sin for sacrifices.</i> the two he-goats<sup class="footnote-marker">47</sup><i class="footnote">There really are three he-goats on that day, the two mentioned in <i>Lev</i>. 16 and the holiday purification offering mentioned in <i>Num</i>. 29:11. The latter is referred to as “he-goat made outside” since its blood is poured onto the altar in the courtyard, where its inner parts are burned. The he-goat chosen as sacrifice by drawing lots is referred to as “he-goat made for inside” since its blood is sprinkled inside the sanctuary (and its body burned outside the sacred domain.) Since there is no reason to treat the holiday purification offering differently from all other holiday offerings, the question asked here must refer to the he-goats subject to drawing lots of which only one is going to be a sacrifice.</i> of the Day of Atonement, there are Tannaim who state, he is liable; there are Tannaim who state, he is not liable. Rav Ḥisda said, he who said that he is liable, if the he-goat who is chosen for inside was sacrificed; he who said that he is not liable, if the he-goat who is chosen for outside was not sacrificed<sup class="footnote-marker">48</sup><i class="footnote">It is clear that for “inside” one has to read “outside” since the question is asked about the he-goat whose blood is to be brought inside, and if it was slaughtered in the Temple it cannot be slaughtered a second time outside. If the he-goat for outside was slaughtered, the main ceremony is concluded <i>Lev</i>. 16:24; the remaining he-goats cannot be sacrifices and their slaughter outside the sacred domain is no offense.</i>. Rebbi Yose said, Rav Ḥisda wants to compare it to <i>Pesaḥ</i> but it is not comparable. Rebbi Mana bar Tanḥum said, Rebbi Eleazar and Rebbi Joḥanan both are saying, a <i>Pesaḥ</i> whose time passed is changed automatically<sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote">A <i>Pesaḥ</i> sacrifice after the 14th of Nisan is a well-being sacrifice. Babli 63a.</i>, but here it changes by slaughter<sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote">The he-goat chosen by the lot cannot be changed into the he-goat for outside.</i>. How is it? He who said liable wanted to say that drawing lots is obstructive; he who said not liable wanted to say that drawing lots is not obstructive<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote">Since the opinion of Rav Ḥisda is refuted, that the Tannaim refer to two different situations and do not disagree, one has to find the root of the disagreement. The text as it stands seems unintelligible; there seems to be unanimity that here also the mentions of “obstructive” and “not obstructive” have to be switched. If drawing is obstructive, neither of the two he-goats is a sacrifice before the drawing, and slaughter outside cannot be sinful. But if it is not obstructive, each one of the he-goats is a potential dedicated sacrifice and outside slaughter is sinful.</i>. There is only one here for Hashem<sup class="footnote-marker">52</sup><i class="footnote">Since only one of the he-goats can become a sacrifice, the argument last given is invalid (unless both he-goats are simultaneously slaughtered outside.)</i>. Rebbi Samuel the brother of Rebbi Berekhiah said, either one of them, after he drew lots is liable for the Eternal’s and is not liable for Azazel’s<sup class="footnote-marker">53</sup><i class="footnote">Since the latter he-goat is not a sacrifice.</i>. Rebbi Abba said, only if he gave the bull’s gift<sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">As described in Mishnah 3, the blood of the bull has to be brought inside. This is called “the gift of the bull’s blood.”</i>. But if he did not give the bull’s gift he is not liable since the slaughter of the he-goat obstructs giving the bull’s blood<sup class="footnote-marker">55</sup><i class="footnote">The he-goat chosen to be the Eternal’s is slaughtered after the bull, but the bull cannot be slaughtered before the he-goat is chosen and ready to be slaughtered.</i>.
Rebbi Abun bar Ḥiyya asked before Rebbi Zeˋira: If he slaughtered the bull before he drew lots, is he liable<sup class="footnote-marker">56</sup><i class="footnote">In the biblical narrative (<i>Lev.</i> 16), first the he-goat has to be selected by drawing lots (v. 8), then the bull has to be slaughtered (v. 11), then first incense (v. 12) and afterwards the bull’s blood (v. 14) have to be brought into the Sanctuary, then the he-goat has to be slaughtered and its blood brought into the sanctuary (v. 15). If the order was reversed and the he-goat selected close to the time of its slaughter, is the ceremony invalid and therefore the slaughter a violation of the prohibition of work on the day of Atonement, and a deadly sin?</i>? He said to him, let us hear from the following: The bull is obstructive of the he-goat, the he-goat is obstructive of the bull<sup class="footnote-marker">57</sup><i class="footnote">Slaughter of the bull is invalid unless the he-goat was selected; slaughter of the he-goat is invalid unless the bull was slaughtered first (and its blood brought inside, Babli 61a).</i>. This implies that if he slaughtered the bull before he drew lots, he is liable. If you would say that he is not liable, one should state, the he-goat is not obstructive of the bull. Rebbi Samuel ben Eudaimon said, that is to say, the he-goat does not obstruct the bull in giving between the beams, but for giving on the curtain the he-goat is obstructive of the bull. How is this? He may not give of the bull’s blood on the curtain before he gave of the he-goat’s blood between the beams<sup class="footnote-marker">58</sup><i class="footnote">The blood has to be sprinkled first inside the Holiest of Holies at the place of the Ark in the First Temple, between the beams used to carry the Ark. In the Second Temple, the place was indicated by a stone, but the terminology was not changed. Then it had to be sprinkled in the Sanctuary onto the gobelin separating it from the Holiest of Holies. Babli 40a.</i>.

Halakhah 2

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> He tied a shiny strip on the head of the he-goat to be sent away<sup class="footnote-marker">59</sup><i class="footnote">Between its horns.</i> and put it next to its departure gate, and on the one to be slaughtered around the place of its slaughter<sup class="footnote-marker">60</sup><i class="footnote">Around its neck, so it clearly would be distinguished from the he-goat chosen for the <i>musaph</i> sacrifice at the end of the service.</i>. He came to his bull a second time, leaned both his hands on it and confessed, and thus he was saying: “Please Hashem, I acted criminally, I offended, I sinned before You, I and my house, and the Sons of Aaron, your holy people. Please Hashem, please atone the criminal acts,” etc<sup class="footnote-marker">61</sup><i class="footnote">The text should be completed by the duly amended text of Mishnah 3:9.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Rebbi Samuel bar Nahman in the name of Rebbi Jonathan: There are three strips<sup class="footnote-marker">62</sup><i class="footnote">Strips of purple wool were used in the Temple not only rabbinically for the he-goats on the day of Atonement but also biblically for the purification ceremony of the person healed from skin disease (<i>Lev.</i>14:4,6) and the preparation of the ashes of the Red Cow (<i>Num.</i> 19:6).</i>. The one for the he-goat for a tetradrachma, for the sufferer from skin disease for a sheqel<sup class="footnote-marker">63</sup><i class="footnote">Rabbinically half a tetradrachma, two denarii. The old Canaanite (biblical) sheqel was about twice as much, cf Qiddušin 1:1, Note 122.</i>, for the Cow for two tetradrachmas. Rebbi Abba bar Zavda in the name of Rebbi Simeon ben Halaphta, for the Cow for two tetradrachmas and a half; some express it in the formulation ten <i>zin</i><sup class="footnote-marker">64</sup><i class="footnote">Defined in <i>Terumot</i> 10:7 (Note 80) as 1/100 of a (probably Roman) pound. 2.5 <i>tetradrachma</i> are 10 <i>denarii.</i> Since an Augustean <i>denar</i> was 1/96 of a Roman pound (silver), 10 <i>zin</i> are 9.6 <i>denarii</i></i>.

Halakhah 3

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> He slaughters it<sup class="footnote-marker">65</sup><i class="footnote">The bull, which is large enough and has enough blood so that the High Priest does not need help in the slaughter.</i> and receives its blood in a pitcher which he hands to one<sup class="footnote-marker">66</sup><i class="footnote">An assisting Cohen.</i> who stirs it on the fourth level<sup class="footnote-marker">67</sup><i class="footnote">There were twelve steps leading from the level of the altar to the entrance of the Temple Hall. Every third step was widened and denoted a level. The fourth, top level was level with the entrance door, so that the High Priest, when he returned from offering the incense, immediately could pick up the blood and re-enter the Temple.</i> of the Temple Hall so it should not congeal<sup class="footnote-marker">68</sup><i class="footnote">After he picks up the incense which is to be given onto the coals inside the Temple. All coals mentioned here are charcoal; mineral coal being unknown at that time.</i>. He took a fire-pan and ascended to the top of the altar where he cleared away coals to both sides and collects coals on the fire pan from the interior well-burned ones, descends, and puts it on the fourth level in the courtyard.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> So is the Mishnah: on the fourth level in the courtyard<sup class="footnote-marker">73</sup><i class="footnote">In the Mishnah, “on the fourth level of the Temple Hall” is identical with “on the fourth level in the courtyard”. It cannot mean “on the fourth level in the Temple Hall” since during the ceremonies of the day of Atonement nobody but the High Priest is permitted to enter the Sanctuary (Lev. 16:17). Babli 43b last line.</i>.
It was stated: If he slaughtered outside he is liable<sup class="footnote-marker">74</sup><i class="footnote">If he slaughtered the bull outside the sacred domain, he is twice liable for extirpation, for violating the holiday and for sacrificing outside. This is obvious and only was stated as contrast to the next statement.</i>, if he took the fistful inside he is not liable<sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in Mishnah 5:1, after he collected the coals other Cohanim bring to him the vessel containing the incense, of which he has to take a fistful and then enter the Sanctuary with the fire pan and the incense. It is difficult to see how he could take the fistful inside since no other Cohen is permitted there on this day, but if he did it the action is valid since there is no verse prescribing that the fistful has to be taken in the courtyard.</i>. If he collected coals and burned the incense when the blood was spilled, he has to bring another bull and enter with its blood<sup class="footnote-marker">76</sup><i class="footnote">Since the verse is clear that incense may be burned only after the bull was slaughtered and that the bull’s blood must be brought inside the Sanctuary after it was filled with incense smoke.</i>. If the blood was spilled before he burned the incense, it is an invalid collection of coals and he has to start again collecting coals. If there was a doubt whether the blood was spilled before he burned the incense or after he burned the incense, you cannot bring another bull and enter with its blood since I am saying that the blood was spilled before he burned the incense and the collection of coals was invalid, and he has to start again collecting coals. You cannot do this since I am saying that the blood was spilled after he burned the incense and the collection of coals was valid, and he is liable because of unnecessary entry. The service has to stop. You find to say, the services of that day are annulled.
If he slaughtered and died<sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:3 requires that Aaron come to the sanctuary <i>with a bull.</i> R. Simeon ben Laqish reads the verse as implying that any other Cohen cannot use his bull’s blood. All other authorities read the same verse as permitting the blood to another Cohen, as explained at the end of the paragraph.</i>. May the other<sup class="footnote-marker">80</sup><i class="footnote">This is the late Amora usually called R. Ḥinena. Babli 49a.</i> enter with his blood. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, <i>with a bull,</i> but not with its blood<sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote">Presuming that somehow the incense did not become impure by the impurity of the dead, may the replacing Cohen use the first’s fistful even though his own fist probably is of different size?</i>. Rebbi Ḥanina and Rebbi Jonathan both are saying, even with the blood. The word of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi implies even with the blood. For Rebbi Ḥanina<sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:12. For the blood it is not written “the blood which he collected”; therefore the blood is transferable.</i>, Rebbi Abba in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan , even with the blood. Rebbi Joshua ben Levi asked, if he took a fistful and then died, may one enter with his fistful<sup class="footnote-marker">83</sup><i class="footnote">Discussion of Mishnah 5.</i>? Why does he question his fistful? For it is written, <i>his fistful</i><sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:8.</i>, but here it is not written “his blood”<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">Standing between the two he-goats, the lot in his right hand is put on the he-goat to his right, and the one in his left on the he-goat to his left side.</i>. It is obvious for him, even with the blood.

Halakhah 4

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Every day he collects coals in a silver fire-pan and empties them into one of gold; on this day he collects in a golden one and takes it inside<sup class="footnote-marker">69</sup><i class="footnote">To make the officiating easier on the High Priest. It is obvious that these silver and gold vessels must have been made of alloys of baser metals to stand the heat.</i>.<br>Every day he collects in one of four <i>qab</i><sup class="footnote-marker">70</sup><i class="footnote">A <i>qab</i> is 2.13 liter, 4 <i>quartarii.</i></i> and empties into one of three <i>qab</i> but on this day he collects in one of three <i>qab</i> which he takes inside. Rebbi Yose says, every day he collects in one of a <i>seah</i><sup class="footnote-marker">71</sup><i class="footnote">6 <i>qab.</i></i> and empties into one of three <i>qab</i> but on this day he collects in one of three <i>qab</i> which he takes inside. Every day it<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote">The fire-pan for the incense, which was adapted to make the High Priest's work easier.</i> was heavy, but this day light. Every day its handle was short, but this day long. Everyday its gold was greenish<sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote">As an alloy with coarse metal; reddish gold probably was a copper alloy.</i>, but this day reddish, the words of Rebbi Menahem.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">83</sup><i class="footnote">Discussion of Mishnah 5.</i> As we have stated there <sup class="footnote-marker">84</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Tamid</i> 5:5, about the daily taking of coals from the altar for the incense burning.</i>: “If about a <i>qab</i> of it was scattered, he swept them into the water canal; but on the Sabbath one covers it with a wine cooler<sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote">Greek ψυκτήρ. The scribe’s spelling is in parentheses, the corrector’s in brackets.</i>.”
“Every day it was heavy, but this day light.” Not to tire him.
“Everyday its handle was short, but this day long.” Not to tire him. Every day it was less that a short cubit<sup class="footnote-marker">93</sup><i class="footnote">It is not clear whether this means a cubit of 5 hand-breadths or one of 6 handbreadths of a small person.</i>, but this day it was a cubit, and a half, so that his arm could lend support. Everyday it did not have a sheath<sup class="footnote-marker">94</sup><i class="footnote">Greek ναρθήκιον. The fire-pan was of metal.</i>, this day it had a sheath, lest he should be burned<sup class="footnote-marker">95</sup><i class="footnote">With Tosaphot 44b <i>s. v</i>. בכל reading יכווה for תכבה.</i>. But does this not separate<sup class="footnote-marker">96</sup><i class="footnote">Since the verse requires that the High Priest carry the fire-pan in his hand (<i>Lev.</i>16:12), nothing may be between his hand and the fire-pan.</i>? Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, it was held by a nail<sup class="footnote-marker">97</sup><i class="footnote">The sheath is an integral part of the pan; this is not separation. According to Tosaphot (44b <i>s.v.</i>בכל יום) this is possible even if the sheath was of leather.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">98</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 44b, <i>Midrash Hazita (Shir rabba)</i> 3(17) on 3:9, <i>Num.</i> rabba 12.</i> There are seven kinds of gold: good gold <sup class="footnote-marker">99</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Gen.</i>2:12.</i>, pure gold<sup class="footnote-marker">100</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ex.</i> 24:11,24; 25:17,32,36,37; 37:2,6</i>, closed gold<sup class="footnote-marker">101</sup><i class="footnote"><i>IK.</i> 7:50.</i>, Mufaz gold<sup class="footnote-marker">102</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Dan.</i> 10:5.</i>, refined gold<sup class="footnote-marker">103</sup><i class="footnote">“Refined” is found in the Bible only applied to silver, see the Halakhah.</i>, drawn gold<sup class="footnote-marker">104</sup><i class="footnote"><i>1K.</i> 10:10, 17, <i>2Chr.</i> 9:15, 16.</i>, Parwayim gold<sup class="footnote-marker">105</sup><i class="footnote"><i>2Chr.</i> 3:6.</i>.
Good gold, as its name says. [<i>And the gold of this land is good.</i><sup class="footnote-marker">99,</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Gen.</i>2:12.</i><sup class="footnote-marker">106</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector's addition, probably from the parallels.</i>] Rebbi Isaac says, it is good to have in one’s house, it is good to accompany one.
Pure gold, which one brings into the fire and nothing is missing. (As) [It comes as]<sup class="footnote-marker">107</sup><i class="footnote">The text in parentheses is the scribe’s (supported by the reliable parallel in <i>Midrash Hazita</i>); the one in brackets is the corrector’s.</i> it was stated: It happened that the golden candelabrum which Moses made in the desert was in excess of one denar, and they returned it to the fire eighty times and it did not lose anything<sup class="footnote-marker">108</sup><i class="footnote">. The text in <i>Midrash Hazita</i> seems original: The candelabrum the of Temple turned out to be in excess of that made in the desert by the weight of a Gordian <i>denar</i>; they refined it in fire 80 times until it lost that extra weight. The weight of the candelabrum itself is not defined in the Bible, only that the candelabrum and all its appurtenances have to be made from one talent (3’000 <i>sheqel)</i> of pure gold.</i>. This is correct. Before it is refined it loses a lot, once it is refined it will not miss anything.
Closed gold, which makes all other kinds of gold look like silver. Rebbi Samuel bar Rav Isaac said, it is written, <i>And seven thousand talents of refined silver to cover the walls of the House</i><sup class="footnote-marker">109</sup><i class="footnote"><i>1Chr.</i> 29:4, in the list of preparations David made for the Temple to be built by Solomon.</i><i>. The entire House he covered with gold</i><sup class="footnote-marker">110</sup><i class="footnote"><i>1K.</i> 6:22, in the report on the actual building of the Temple.</i><i>,</i> and you are saying so<sup class="footnote-marker">111</sup><i class="footnote">Why is silver suddenly called gold?</i>? But it was making all other kinds of gold look like silver.
Mufaz gold. Rebbi Patroki the brother of Rebbi Drosa in the name of Rebbi Abba bar Bina: It looks like fire which was kindled with sulphur. Rebbi Abbin, it is called after its place, <i>and gold from Ufaz</i><sup class="footnote-marker">112</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Jer.</i> 10:9.</i><i>.</i>
Refined gold, one was cutting it up like olives, form it into dough, and feed it to ostriches; they filter it. But some are saying, that they were burying it in manure for seven years.
Drawn gold. It could be drawn like wax. Hadrian had the weight of an egg of it. Diocletian had the weight of a Gordian denar<sup class="footnote-marker">113</sup><i class="footnote">One of the few coins minted during the inflationary period of the military anarchy in the Roman Empire with a reputation of being honest. Cf. D. Sperber, <i>Roman Palestine</i>200–400 <i>Money and Prices,</i> Ramat Gan 1974.</i> of it.
Parwayim gold. Rebbi Simeon ben Laqish said, red, it is like ox blood, but some are saying, gold which produces fruits. As we have stated there<sup class="footnote-marker">114</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Middot</i> 3:5. Babli 21b.</i>, “a golden vine was standing at the door of the inner hall.” Rebbi Aḥa bar Isaac said, at the time when Solomon built the Temple, he formed all kinds of trees in it and at the time when those outside where bearing fruit, those inside where bearing fruit. That is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">115</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Is.</i> 35:2.</i>, <i>blooming the blossom and jubilate, also enjoying and singing,</i> etc. When did they dry up? Rebbi Isaac Ḥinena bar Isaac said, when Manasse put up at statue in the Temple they dried up, as it is written, <i>and the flower of the Lebanon is wilted</i><sup class="footnote-marker">116</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Nah.</i> 1:4. For “Lebanon” as sobriquet for the Temple cf, <i>IK.</i> 7:2.</i><i>.</i>

Halakhah 5

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Every day he sacrifices one half<sup class="footnote-marker">88</sup><i class="footnote">Latin <i>pars, -rtis, f</i> The full portion was the weight of one <i>mina,</i> or 25/24 of a Roman pound (cf. Note 64).</i> in the morning and one half in the evening, but on this day he adds a fistful<sup class="footnote-marker">89</sup><i class="footnote">The incense to be burned in the Holiest of Holies, in contrast to the larger amount burned on the incense altar in the sanctuary.</i>. Every day it was fine but this day finese<sup class="footnote-marker">90</sup><i class="footnote">Incense to be burned on the altar is just called “incense” but the one destined for the Holiest of Holies has to be “fine incense” (Lev. I 6:8); it is inferred that it has to be finer than regular incense.</i>. Every day the Cohanim ascend on the East side {of the ramp} and descend on the West side, but this day they<sup class="footnote-marker">91</sup><i class="footnote">“They” are only the High Priest, who this day does the sacral acts unaided. There is no danger of a traffic jam.</i> ascend and descend in the middle. Rebbi Jehudah says, the High Priest always ascends in the middle and descendes in the middle.<br>Every day the High Priest sanctifies his hands and legs from the basin put this day from a gold pitcher<sup class="footnote-marker">92</sup><i class="footnote">Identified by Buxtorf as Latin <i>cothon,</i> Greek κώθων, but this denotes a drinking vessel, not a pitcher.</i>. Rebbi Jehudah says, always the High Priest sanctifies his hands and legs from a gold pitcher.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">117</sup><i class="footnote">Babli <i>Keritut</i>6a/b.</i> The compounding of the incense: balsamum, and cloves, galbanum and frankincense, each in the weight of 70 <i>maneh</i><sup class="footnote-marker">118</sup><i class="footnote">It is not obvious whether the reference is to the Semitic <i>maneh</i>, 60 <i>šeqel</i>, or the Greek <i>mnā</i>, 100 <i>denar</i> (<i>drachmē</i>). In the rabbinic system 1 <i>šeqel</i> = 2 <i>denar</i>. Since in all other circumstances we find that מנה denotes 100 <i>denar</i> (weight or money) there is no reason to assume that here the situation is different, even though the traditional vocalization in this context is מָנֶה.</i><i>.</i> Myrrh and cassia, spicenard and saffron, each in the weight of sixteen <i>maneh.</i> Costus twelve, bark three, cinnamon nine. You find that there were 365 <i>maneh</i> according to the days of the year and three for this day<sup class="footnote-marker">119</sup><i class="footnote">The total amount adds up to 368 <i>maneh</i>.</i>. That is what we have stated: “but on this day he adds a fistful.” Carshina<sup class="footnote-marker">120</sup><i class="footnote">Name of a plant, usually leeks (in Arabic, peas or a related vegetable.) In the Babli, “Carshina lye“; as shown by the next paragraph, this must be the reading here also. <i>Qab</i> as a volume is a fluid measure.</i> nine <i>qab,</i> (Qanrisin) [caper]<sup class="footnote-marker">121</sup><i class="footnote">The text in parentheses is the scribe’s, the one in brackets the corrector’s. Since the scribe was very consistent in his spelling of the name, this is not a scribal error and the corrector’s has to be classified as copied from the Babli. The word used by the scribe is a hapax, its meaning is unknown. If it is from قنّار “small onions”, the meaning of the Yerushalmi term is close to the of the Babli, wine with added vegetable aroma.</i> wine three <i>seah</i> and three <i>qab.</i> If he has no (Qanrisin) [caper] wine he brings aged whitish wine. Sodom salt<sup class="footnote-marker">122</sup><i class="footnote">Dead Sea salt.</i> a quarter. Some smoke producing herb. Rebbi Nathan says, also some (Qafra) [Kifa]<sup class="footnote-marker">123</sup><i class="footnote">Here also the corrector’s version in brackets is the Babli text, against the scribe’s in parentheses. An aromatic plant also mentioned in Tosephta <i>Demai</i> 1:29 (cf. S.Liebermann, <i>Tosefta ki-fshutah, Zeraim</i> vol, 1, New York 1955, p. 208).</i> of the Jordan. If he added honey he invalidated it. If he left out one of its ingredients he is liable for death<sup class="footnote-marker">124</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 53a.<br>Again spelling of corrector following the Babli. Probably the Babylonian pronunciation of <i>qtaf</i> was close to the Galilean of <i>qtav</i>. עֵץ can mean both “tree” and “bush”.</i>.
It was stated: Rabban Simeon ben Gamliel says, balsamum is only the sap of the (qtab) [qtaf]<sup class="footnote-marker">124</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 53a.<br>Again spelling of corrector following the Babli. Probably the Babylonian pronunciation of <i>qtaf</i> was close to the Galilean of <i>qtav</i>. עֵץ can mean both “tree” and “bush”.</i> tree. For what comes Carshina lye? In it one polished the cloves. For what does (Qanrisin) [caper] wine come? In it one (polishes) [soaks]<sup class="footnote-marker">125</sup><i class="footnote">Here the correction of the corrector following the Babli seems to be correct.</i> cloves that it should be strong. Would not be urine good for this? Only one does not introduce bad smell into the Temple courtyard because of decorum<sup class="footnote-marker">126</sup><i class="footnote">Babli <i>Roš Haššanah</i> 32a.</i>. And when he was pulverizing he was saying: be well pulverized, be well pulverized, for voice is good for compounding. If he left out one of its ingredients or added honey he invalidated it. If he failed to add salt<sup class="footnote-marker">127</sup><i class="footnote">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i>20a.</i> or added<sup class="footnote-marker">128</sup><i class="footnote">Obviously this must read “did not add”. Babli 53a.</i> smoke producing herb he became liable for death. Rebbi Zeˋura said, and he sins because of unnecessary entry<sup class="footnote-marker">129</sup><i class="footnote">If the incense is disqualified, entering the Sanctuary with it is sinful.</i>.
It was stated: Bar Qappara said, the perfumers in Jerusalem were saying, if one would add some honey, the entire world could not withstand its smell.
It was stated: If one compounded half of it it is qualified. Thirds and quarters we did not hear. Rebbi said, in its proportion it is qualified. Therefore, what one said, if one compounded half of it it is qualified, half of every ingredient. Once in sixty or seventy years half of it was coming from leftovers. That is, “what was one doing with excess incense”<sup class="footnote-marker">130</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Šeqalim</i> 4:5. The Mishnah implies that leftover incense powder at the end of the year was a common occurrence.</i>?
It was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">131</sup><i class="footnote">Babli <i>Zevahim</i> 109a.</i>: If he burned<sup class="footnote-marker">132</sup><i class="footnote">Of incense correctly compounded.</i> the size of an olive outside he is liable; less than the volume of an olive inside he is not liable<sup class="footnote-marker">133</sup><i class="footnote">“Not liable” usually means “forbidden but not punishable.” The Babli, probably more correctly, has: less than a <i>pars</i> (Note 90).</i>. Rebbi Zeˋira in the name of Rav Jeremiah<sup class="footnote-marker">134</sup><i class="footnote">The first generation. Babylonian Amora.</i>: The public has fulfilled its obligation<sup class="footnote-marker">135</sup><i class="footnote">Since no weights or measures are given in the biblical text.</i>. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun in the name of Rebbi Jeremiah<sup class="footnote-marker">136</sup><i class="footnote">The student of R. Zeˋira.</i>, since it was stated that if he burned the size of an olive outside he is liable, from this you infer that less than the volume of an olive inside he is not liable<sup class="footnote-marker">137</sup><i class="footnote">If he only is liable for a full olive-sized amount outside, he cannot be liable for less than an olive-sized piece inside. If this is formulated as separate statement, it must mean that he is not liable and the action is irrelevant. The statement of Rav Jeremiah must be in the Babylonian tradition referring to a <i>pars</i>.</i>.
<i>Fine</i><sup class="footnote-marker">138</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev</i>. 16:12.</i>. What does the verse say? Because it was said, <i>you shall pulverize it finely</i><sup class="footnote-marker">139</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ex</i>. 31:36. If the entire year the incense must be a fine powder, what does the remark mean that on the Day of Atonement it be fine?</i>. Then why is it said, <i>fine</i>? That it be most fine. What does he do? He separates the <i>mina</i> on the Eve of the Day of Atonement and returns it to the mortar to fill from it his fistful to observe “most fine.<sup class="footnote-marker">140</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 45a, <i>Keritut</i>_6b.</i>”
Rebbi Jonah said, except for the first sanctification<sup class="footnote-marker">141</sup><i class="footnote">This now refers to Mishnah 8, that the High Priest does not use the basin but a golden pitcher. Since the first sanctification from the basis is a biblical requirement (<i>Ex</i>. 30:20–21, 40:30) it cannot be waved.</i>. Rebbi Yose said, even for the first sanctification. A <i>baraita</i> disagrees with Rebbi Jonah: All vessels<sup class="footnote-marker">142</sup><i class="footnote">All containers. <i>Zevaḥim</i> 21b/22a.</i> in the Temple were qualified for sanctifying hands and legs. He explains it, except for the first sanctification. A <i>baraita</i> disagrees with Rebbi Yose: the basin and its base are obstructive. He explains it, their place is obstructive<sup class="footnote-marker">143</sup><i class="footnote">The place between the Tent of Meeting and the altar (<i>Ex</i>. 30:18). If the basin is not in its place, no service can be held.</i>.

Halakhah 6

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Every day there were four arrangements<sup class="footnote-marker">144</sup><i class="footnote">The formal arrangement of wood on the altar. For R. Meïr the first one is in the morning for the daily sacrifice, the second for taking charcoal for the daily burning of incense on the interior altar, the third to make sure the fire is not extinguished for the remainder of the day, the fourth to burn through the night.</i> and this day five<sup class="footnote-marker">145</sup><i class="footnote">Additional logs from which the High Priest takes charcoal to bring into the Holiest of Holies.</i>, the words of Rebbi Meïr. Rebbi Yose says, everyday three and this day four. Rebbi Jehudah says, every day two and this day three.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> What is Rebbi Meïr’s reason? <sup class="footnote-marker">148</sup><i class="footnote">He holds that any Sanctuary fire can be made only on top of the outer altar, including the one used to light the candelabrum. Babli 45b.</i><i>And the fire on the altar shall be lit there, you shall not extinguish</i>, that is the arrangement which keeps the fire. <i>And the Cohen shall burn on it</i>, that is the arrangement for disposal of limbs and fat. <i>And arrange on it the elevation sacrifice</i>, this is the main arrangement. <i>And burn as incense on it the fats of the well-being sacrifices</i>, this is the incense. Rebbi Yose does not have the arrangement for disposal of limbs. Rebbi Jehudah does not have the arrangement which keeps the fire. How does Rebbi Jehudah explain <i>a permanent fire</i><sup class="footnote-marker">147</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev</i>. 6:6.</i>? The fire which I told you that it be permanent only shall be on the outer altar<sup class="footnote-marker">148</sup><i class="footnote">He holds that any Sanctuary fire can be made only on top of the outer altar, including the one used to light the candelabrum. Babli 45b.</i>.
Rebbi Eleazar said, limbs and fat which were not consumed before the evening one builds into a pyre<sup class="footnote-marker">149</sup><i class="footnote">On the altar.</i> and burns them separately; for them one pushes aside the Sabbath<sup class="footnote-marker">150</sup><i class="footnote">The remainders of Friday sacrifices have to be burned in the following night which is Sabbath.</i>. Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa in the name of Rebbi Samuel bar Abba: The Mishnah implies this: “Every day there were four arrangements.” What does one understand from here<sup class="footnote-marker">151</sup><i class="footnote">Maybe “every day” excludes Friday evening.</i>? Rebbi Mana said, “and this day five<sup class="footnote-marker">152</sup><i class="footnote">Since everything forbidden on the Sabbath is forbidden on the Day of Atonement (Mishnah <i>Megillah</i> 1:5), if the special arrangement for the night is prescribed for the day of Atonement it also must be prescribed for the Sabbath.</i>”. Rebbi Abun bar Ḥiyya asked before Rebbi Zeˋira: May something which is not obstructive push aside<sup class="footnote-marker">153</sup><i class="footnote">Since the sacrifice is valid if the blood was poured on the walls of the altar, the later disposal cannot invalidate. If one would leave the remainders unburned and after the Sabbath burn them outside the sacred domain, everything would remain valid. Why should the Sabbath be pushed aside for this, even though it has biblical justification?</i>? He answered him, there are the witnesses for the New Moon who are not obstructive<sup class="footnote-marker">154</sup><i class="footnote">Even in times when the New Moon was proclaimed on the basis of testimony, the Supreme Court had the possibility of declaring the New Moon based on their computations (Mishnah <i>Roš Haššanah</i> 2:11.</i> and push aside, as we have stated there<sup class="footnote-marker">155</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Roš Haššanah</i> 1:11.</i>: “for a distance of a night and day one desecrates the Sabbath and comes for testimony of the New Moon.”
From where the arrangement of the Day of Atonement<sup class="footnote-marker">156</sup><i class="footnote">That the wood on the altar has to be prepared specially for the requirements of the day and therefore needs an extra arrangement, in addition to the daily ones.</i>? Rebbi Jeremiah in the name of Rebbi Pedat: <i>Coals</i><sup class="footnote-marker">157</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev</i>. 16:12.</i>. Why does the verse say, <i>of fire?</i> That it should be insignificant on its coals. <sup class="footnote-marker">158</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Sifra Aḥare Pereq</i> 3(5); Babli <i>Pesaḥim</i> 75b.. The following text is Tannaitic, not of the sayings of R. Jeremiah. It is missing in a Genizah fragment (Ginzberg, p. 118) and therefore may be a later addition. This explains the reduplication of the argument.</i>“<i>Coals</i>, I could think smouldering; the verse says <i>of fire</i>. If <i>of fire</i>, I could think flames; the verse says <i>coals of fire</i>, from those crackling ones. And from where that the fire should be insignificant on the coals? The verse says, <i>coals of fire</i>.”
Rebbi Joshua ben Levi said, the shew-bread did not become disqualified during travel time<sup class="footnote-marker">159</sup><i class="footnote">Since the shew-bread has to be on the table in the Sanctuary (<i>Lev</i>. 24:5–9) it is obvious that bread taken out of a stationary Sanctuary becomes disqualified. The question is whether it also became disqualified when the Sanctuary around it was removed by divine command during the wanderings of he Israelites in the desert.</i>. [Rebbi Joḥanan said, the shew-bread became disqualified during travel time.]<sup class="footnote-marker">160</sup><i class="footnote">Addition by the corrector; sentence missing in the Genizah fragment published by Ginzberg (Note 159). The Babli, <i>Menaḥot</i>95a, reports a disagreement of R. Joshua ben Levi and R. Joḥanan about this subject.</i> Rebbi Ḥiyya in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi: <i>just as they camped so they travelled</i><sup class="footnote-marker">161</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Num</i>. 2:17.</i>, since it did not become disqualified when they were camping so it did not become disqualified when they were travelling. Rebbi Immi in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi: <i>The Tent of Meeting, the encampment of the Levites, shall travel in the midst of</i><sup class="footnote-marker">161</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Num</i>. 2:17.</i><i>camps</i>, as if in the center of camps.
Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa, Rebbi Immi in the name of Rebbi Eleazar: One who burns <i>sancta</i> outside during travel time is flogged<sup class="footnote-marker">162</sup><i class="footnote">Private altars and sacrifices outside the central sanctuary are forbidden, <i>Lev</i>. 17. In the absence of a central sanctuary, private altars are permitted, Mishnah <i>Zevaḥim</i> 14:4–8. If a central Sanctuary exists but is temporarily unavailable, the prohibition remains in place; <i>Menaḥot</i>95a.</i>. Rebbi Joḥanan said, <i>sancta</i> became rejects during travel time<sup class="footnote-marker">163</sup><i class="footnote">Sacrifices must either be burned on the altar in the courtyard of the Sanctuary or eaten within sanctified enclosures. If all enclosures are removed, all leftovers of sacrifices are automatically disqualified. Babli <i>Zevaḥim</i> 60b as tannaitic statement.</i>; the impure remain separated each one according to his partition<sup class="footnote-marker">164</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Num</i>. 5:1–4. A person suffering from gonorrhea is excluded from the dwelling of the Levites, a sufferer from skin disease also from the camp of the Israelites. Since they were marching in military order, the impure were excluded from the marching order. Babli <i>Zevaḥim</i> 60b as tannaitic statement.</i>. Rebbi Yose said, the following is frequent in the mouth of the rabbis: When the gobelins were removed, the partitions were permitted to sufferers from gonorrhea and skin disease<sup class="footnote-marker">165</sup><i class="footnote">During travel times there is no inside and the impure cannot be sent outside.</i>. A <i>baraita</i> supports the one and a <i>baraita</i> supports the other.<sup class="footnote-marker">166</sup><i class="footnote">Since R. Joshua ben Levi is not mentioned in the present paragraph, the reference to him has to be to the preceding one. The reference to R. Joḥanan is incomprehensible; the quoted <i>baraita</i> does not refer to any previous statement but to the following of R. Jehudah.</i> A <i>baraita</i><sup class="footnote-marker">167</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Sifra Ṣaw Pereq</i> 2(10), a <i>baraita</i> of R. Jehudah. Anywhere “permanent” is mentioned, it overrides restrictions. Since “permanent” is mentioned for the fire of that altar, <i>Lev</i>. 6:6, the priests have to tend the fire on the Sabbath even if all of them are impure. But “permanent” also is mentioned for the shew-bread (<i>Lev</i>. 24:8); this overrides the absence of the walls of the Sanctuary. By the same token, R. Joshua ben Levi has to hold that the altar fire has to be tended on the march; following R. Jehudah in the sequel.</i> supports Rebbi Joshua ben Levi: “<i>Permanent</i>, even on the Sabbath; <i>permanent</i> even in impurity.” A <i>baraita</i> supports Rebbi Joḥanan , “<i>you shall not extinguish it</i>, even during travel<sup class="footnote-marker">168</sup><i class="footnote">Continuation of <i>Sifra Ṣaw Pereq</i> 2(10) on <i>Lev</i>. 6:6.</i>. What did they do [at travel time]<sup class="footnote-marker">169</sup><i class="footnote">Addition by the corrector; it should be deleted since by removing it the sentence and the next are again continuation of <i>Sifra Ṣaw Pereq</i> 2(10).</i>? They put a wine-cooler<sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote">As an alloy with coarse metal; reddish gold probably was a copper alloy.</i> over it, the words of Rebbi Jehudah. Rebbi Simeon says, even at travel time they were removing ashes from it, as it is said<sup class="footnote-marker">170</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Num</i>. 4:13.</i>, <i>they shall remove the ashes from the altar and spread a purple cloth over it</i>.” If the altar were burning, would the purple cloth not be burned? What does Rebbi Jehudah do with this? They put a wine-cooler over it. How does Rebbi Jehudah validate <i>they shall remove the ashes from the altar</i>? They shall saturate it; as Rebbi Jehudah ben Pazi said, <i>he ate, and was sated, and saturated</i><sup class="footnote-marker">171</sup><i class="footnote">In all cognate languages דשן, دسم means “to be fat”. The use of דשן as “ashes” must mean “ashes from fatty material”. R. Jehudah will not extend the extended meaning of the noun to the corresponding verb.</i>.

Chapter 5



Halakhah 1

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> They brought him the cup and the pan<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Other Cohanim bring him an empty cup and the censer full of the incense specially prepared for this day.</i>; he took his full fistfuls and put it into the cup, a big person according to his bigness, and a small person according to his smallness, this was their measure. He took the fire-pan<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">With the hot coals, which he had deposited on the uppermost step at the entrance to the Temple.</i> into his right hand and the cup in his left, went into the Temple until he reached the space between the two gobelins which separate between the Holy and the Holiest of Holies with one cubit between them. Rebbi Yose says, there was only one gobelin as it was said<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ex.</i> 26:33.</i>, <i>and the gobelin shall separate for you between the Holy and the Holiest of Holies</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “They brought him the cup,” etc. But was it not already stated<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah 4:3. The same expression מַתְתָּה is used in Mishnah 4:3 and in 5:1. But if the High Priest already used the מַתְתָּה before, it cannot be brought to him now from a storage facility.</i>, “he took a fire-pan and ascended to the top of the altar”? So is the Mishnah: The cup and the bowl. What is a כַּף? A tureen<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">From a rabbinic Hebrew root מגיס “to stir, to mix dough” which may have been induced by Greek μαγίς “dough”.</i>. Rebbi Yose said, this implies that it is a profane vessel. If you would say, a sanctified vessel, may something sanctified in a vessel be redeemed<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">This would contradict <i>Lev.</i> 27:10 stating that anything dedicated and fit for Divine service may not be redeemed.</i>?
<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">The incense used in the Temple.</i> As they disagreed: If it was compounded as profane, Rebbi Yose ben Ḥanina said, it is disqualified; Rebbi Joshua ben Levi said, it is qualified. What is Rebbi Yose ben Ḥanina’s reason? <i>It is holy</i><sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">There is no such verse; similar verses about incense would be <i>Ex.</i> 30:36, <i>most holy it shall be for you, Ex.</i> 30:37, <i>holy it shall be for you.</i> Babli <i>Keritut</i> 6a.</i><i>,</i> that it shall be brought into the Sanctuary<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">It seems that the correct text is in <i>Šeqalim:</i> That its existence shall be in the holy space. The Babli text there adds: “and it shall be brought from the contributions to the treasury,” i. e., from the Temple tax.</i>. What is Rebbi Joshua ben Levi’s reason? <i>It is holy,</i> that it shall be brought from the contributions to the treasury<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">In the Babli text: “that it shall be brought into the Sanctuary” which in our text is the <i>Yoma</i> version of R. Yose ben Ḥanina. In the Babli <i>Šeqalim</i> text it makes sense; the preparation may be in profane terrain, only the use must be in the Sanctuary.</i>. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Bun said, Rebbi Yose ben Ḥanina’s parallels Samuel and Rebbi Joshua ben Levi’s Rebbi Joḥanan , as we have stated, “if one dedicated his property to the Temple and there were objects appropriate as public offerings<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Šeqalim</i> 4:6.</i>.” Rebbi Joḥanan said, incense. Rebbi Hoshaia said, explain it about an artisan of the family Eutinos [who took incense as his wages.<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">Addition of the corrector from <i>Šeqalim.</i> As explained in <i>Šeqalim,</i> incense of each year has to bought by the proceeds of the Temple tax of that year. In order to avoid that any leftovers at the end of the year became disqualified, the leftovers are given to the workers and artisans working for the Temple as their wages. The Temple can then buy back the incense from the workers with money of the next year and the incense remains qualified. (Private use of incense compounded by the Temple’s formula is a deadly sin, <i>Ex.</i> 30:38.) R. Joḥanan ’s argument that the Mishnah can only be interpreted as referring to incense is given in the Babli, <i>Keritut</i> 6a.</i>] And Rebbi Joshua ben Levi’s is like Samuel, as Rebbi Ḥuna<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">Read with <i>Šeqalim:</i> Rav Ḥuna.</i> said in the name of Samuel, they made the mortar a vessel of sacred service<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">Here one has to read with the Babli <i>Šeqalim:</i> did <i>not</i> make. The incense always is prepared in a profane vessel; it becomes dedicated by being used on the dedicated fire-pan or the interior altar.</i>. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, Rebbi Ḥuna said this before Rebbi Yose: something sanctified in a vessel may be redeemed<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">Answering his question in the negative. R. Yose holds that practice does not follow Samuel.</i>. He said to him, is that not Samuel’s? Since Samuel said, it is slight in the case of leftovers<sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote">Animals and supplies bought with Temple tax monies but not used by the end of a fiscal year, which cannot be used for the next year.</i>. As they disagreed: If daily sacrifices were left over, Samuel says, they are redeemed unblemished<sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote">It is impossible to redeem animals qualified to be sacrifices, <i>Lev.</i> 27:10. Samuel proposes to treat the surplus animals similar to how surplus incense was treated: The animals are redeemed with the past year’s excess money, which then is used for repair or improvement of the Temple building as explained in <i>Šeqalim</i> Chapter 4. Then the animals are bought again with money of the new fiscal year and become newly qualified.</i>. Rebbi Joḥanan said, they are redeemed as disqualified <i>sancta</i><sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote">He requires that the excess sheep be let grazing until either they develop a defect or become disqualified by age; then they may be redeemed like any other disqualified animal. A different tradition Babli <i>Ševuot</i>11b.</i><i>.</i> Leftover he-goats<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote">Bought for public purification sacrifices on holidays and days of the New Moon.</i>, in Samuel’s opinion if elevation sacrifices are redeemed, a purification sacrifice so much more. In Rebbi Joḥanan ’s opinion? Rebbi Zeˋira said, they shall graze<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote">Same procedure as for sheep, Note 24.</i>. Rebbi Samuel bar Rav Isaac said, one uses them to adorn the altar<sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote">To be used as elevation offerings in periods where the altar otherwise would be empty. These sacrifices not being obligatory cannot be bought with money from the Temple tax; one uses dedicated animals which are not being used for their original purpose. The statement is erroneously missing in the Babli <i>Šeqalim.</i></i>. This is difficult. May a purification sacrifice be brought as elevation sacrifice? Rebbi Yose said, there is a difference, for public sacrifices are determined only by slaughter<sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote">If they never had been dedicated as purification sacrifices, the rules of the latter do not apply. Accepted as opinion both by Samuel and R. Joḥanan in Babli <i>Ševuot</i> 12b.</i>. Rebbi Ḥananiah ben Tradion<sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote">With the <i>Šeqalim</i> texts delete the last two words; the tradent is a late Amora not the early Tanna..</i> said, it is a stipulation of the Court that all leftovers should be brought as elevation sacrifices<sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote">Since the stipulation preceded the acquisition of the animals by the Temple, R. Yose’s answer is unnecessary.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 47a, <i>Menaḥot</i>11a, <i>Sifra Wayyiqra I Parshata</i> 9(6).</i>“<i>His full handful</i><sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev</i>. 2:2.</i>. I could assume an overstuffed handful, the verse says, <i>with his handful</i><sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev</i>. 6:8.</i>. If <i>with his handful,</i> I could assume that he picks it up with his finger tips, the verse says, <i>his full handful.</i> How is this? He sinks his hand into the baking pan<sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev</i>. 2:5.</i> or frying pan<sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev</i>. 2:7.</i> and wipes clean with his finger from top to bottom.”
There, you are saying, <i>his full handful, with his handful,</i> and here you are saying, <i>his full handful</i><sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote">The following text implies that here one has to read וּמְלֹ֣א חָפְנָ֔יו (<i>Lev.</i> 16:12), the expression used for the service of the Day of Atonement. It is asserted that the meaning of חָפְנַיִם used in Chapter 16 is identical with קוֹמֶץ used in Chapters 2 and 6, except naturally that the קוֹמֶץ, used in the singular, refers to his right hand only whereas the חָפְנַיִם need both hands.</i><i>.</i> Rebbi Jacob bar Aḥa, Rebbi Simon in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi, since there a deficient handful is disqualified, here also a deficient handful is disqualified. Are his fists considered vessels of service to sanctify<sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote">The paragraph is R. Joshua ben Levi’s teaching, who asserted before that the incense is compounded in a profane vessel. The question then arises at which moment the incense becomes sanctified to be used in the Temple service, in the hand of the High Priest when he takes it out of the profane cup or in the bowl in which he deposits it. The bowl certainly is a Temple vessel only used for sanctified contents.</i>? May another person take the fistful and puts it in his fist<sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 49a.</i>? Should it be made to measure for his fists<sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote">“It” is the empty bowl into which the High Priest deposits his fistful of incense. The next sentence really is a repetition of the question here, whether the same vessel is used for all High Priests or not.</i>? Do you estimate for all possible fists or you estimate for his fist only? Rebbi Joshua ben Levi asked: If he took a fistful and died, may another person enter with his fistful<sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote">May his successor use his incense, presuming it did not become impure by the death. Babli 49a.</i>? If you are saying that they did not consider his fists a vessel of service of the Sanctuary, this implies that another person may enter with his fistful; another person may take the fistful and put it in his fist; one makes to measure for his fists; one does not estimate for all possible fists<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote">If only the bowl turns the incense into dedicated material, taking the fistful is a necessary action but must not necessarily be done by him personally; therefore also the successor may continue to use the incense taken by the first High Priest. But it is necessary to switch the last two statements, “one makes to measure for his fists; one does not estimate for all possible fists” to the case that his fists are consecrating, and read here “one does not make to measure for his fists; one estimates for all possible fists.”</i>. If you are saying that they considered his fists a vessel of service of the Sanctuary, this implies that another person may not enter with his fistful; another person may not take the fistful and put in his fist; one does not make to measure for his fists; one estimates for all possible fists.
“A big person according to his bigness,” even like Ben Qimḥit whose hand contained about four <i>qab</i><sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote">About 8 liter.</i>, “and a small person according to his smallness,” even like Ben Gamia, whose hand contained only about two olives.
What is the status of motion by an Non-Cohen<sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote">This question cannot be about the Day of Atonement, where not even an ordinary Cohen may perform one of the duties of the High Priest, but of the regular service in the Temple, except those where the verse explicitly prescribes that a Cohen has to move the object; cf. <i>Lev.</i> 1:15.</i>? Ḥizqiah said, motion by a Non-Cohen is qualified. Rebbi Yannai said, motion by a Non-Cohen is disqualified. A Mishnah disagrees with Rebbi Yannai<sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Zevaḥim</i> 3:2. As a rule, sacral acts by the priests have to be performed with their right hands. Therefore the blood of a sacrifice has to be collected by the Cohen in a sacred vessel held in his right hand; if later he temporarily switches the vessel to his left hand he may return it to his right hand and it remains qualified.</i>: “If he received with his right hand and put it in his left hand, he shall return it to his right hand.” Is his left hand not like a Non-Cohen? Explain it if his left hand was towards the inside<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote">If he returns the vessel to the right hand he increases its distance from the altar; this is not part of the transport of the blood to the altar.</i>. Rebbi Abba said, even if you are saying, towards the outside, there is a difference between motion by a Non-Cohen and one which is automatic. Rebbi Zeˋira said, they did not consider a movement of his hand as motion. A Mishnah disagrees with Rebbi Yannai:<sup class="footnote-marker">46</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Zevaḥim</i> 3:2.</i> “If from the vessel something was spilled on the floor and he collected it, it is qualified.” Rebbi Bevai said, explain it if it was rolling towards the inside. Rebbi Abba said, even if you are saying towards the outside, there is a difference between motion by a Non-Cohen and one which is automatic. Rebbi Zeˋira said, they did consider a movement of his hand as motion. The Mishnah disagrees with Rebbi Yannai: “He took the fire-pan<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">With the hot coals, which he had deposited on the uppermost step at the entrance to the Temple.</i> into his right hand and the cup in his left.” There is a difference because he cannot do it otherwise. Should he hang it on his arm? It is not respectful. May he switch? They wanted to say<sup class="footnote-marker">47</sup><i class="footnote">The unanimous opinion of the members of the Academy although there is no tannaitic statement to guide the decision.</i>, if he switched it was disqualified. Should he lower it<sup class="footnote-marker">48</sup><i class="footnote">Put the vessel in his left hand under the right hand to support the right hand.</i>? If he lowered it from his right hand to his left hand it is qualified. Could we say that also there<sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote">Can one say in the case from <i>Zevaḥim</i> that the vessel could remain in his left hand if it is held on his right hand side below his right hand?</i>, let him lower it? There if he lowered it it is disqualified. [If he switched it is disqualified.]<sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote">Addition by the corrector; correct but not absolutely necessary.</i> But here if he lowered it it is qualified; if he switched it is disqualified<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote">If the fire pan is in his left hand and the cup with the dry incense powder in his right hand.</i>.
Everybody agrees that if he brought them inside one by one, he atoned, but he transgresses because of unnecessary entry<sup class="footnote-marker">52</sup><i class="footnote">An unnecessary entry into the Holiest of Holies is a deadly sin, <i>Lev.</i> 16:2.</i>. About which one does he transgress? The colleagues say, about the last one. Rebbi Yose said to him, one tells him to enter and you are saying so? But it is about the first one. There, we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">53</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Ševuot</i> 2:4 (Note 60). The text there, reported in slightly different formulation, seems to be the correct one: “How is that? About which of them does he become liable? About the first or the last? The colleagues say, about the first. Rebbi Yose told them, one says to him, leave, and you say about the first? But we must hold about the last.” The improper behavior was that he tarried, not that he entered when pure. This parallels the first case, where the first entry was necessary and therefore legitimate, only the second one is unnecessary and sinful.</i>: “If he prostrated himself, or tarried that he could have prostrated himself, or left on a lengthy path, he is liable<sup class="footnote-marker">60</sup><i class="footnote">In this and the next sentence, the places of “R. Yose” and “the rabbis” have to be switched since the simple meaning of the verse supports R. Yose. Tosephta 2:12.</i>.” About which one is he liable? The colleagues say, about the first one. Rebbi Yose said to him, one tells him to leave and you are saying so? But it is about the last one.
“With one cubit between them.” Rebbi Hila said, this<sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">That in contrast to the First temple, the Second had two gobelins, the interior one belonging to the Holiest of Holies and the exterior one belonging to the Temple Hall, with a cubit in between. The problem whether the cubit between interior and exterior gobelins belongs to the Temple Hall or the Holies of Holies is quoted as undecidable in <i>Kilaim</i> 8:5 where part of the text is found (Notes 93–95) and Babli 52a.</i> is hinted at as we have stated there<sup class="footnote-marker">55</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Middot</i> 4:7.</i>, “One cubit <i>taraqsin,</i> twenty cubits for the building of the Holiest of Holies.” What is “one cubit <i>taraqsin”?</i> Rebbi Jonah from Bostra said, “confusion”, what is inside-outside<sup class="footnote-marker">56</sup><i class="footnote">Jastrow’s conjecture that טרקסין is Greek τάραξιν, accusative of τάραξις, “confusion”; cf. <i>Kilaim</i> 8:5 Note 93.</i>. Rebbi Yose said, since it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">57</sup><i class="footnote"><i>1K.</i> 6:17.</i>, <i>forty cubits was the House, that is the inner Temple,</i> it means that it is counted inside. Rebbi Mana said to him, but it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">58</sup><i class="footnote"><i>2Chr.</i> 3:8. Since the reports about the first Temple do not mention the cubit in between, all they prove is that the interior gobelin belongs to the Holiest of Holies and the exterior one to the Temple Hall.</i>, <i>he made the building of the Holiest of Holies,…, twenty cubits,</i> it means that it is counted outside. What is the rabbis’ reason? <i>The gobelin shall separate for you</i><sup class="footnote-marker">59</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ex.</i> 26:33. This is R. Yose’s (the Tanna) reason that only one gobelin is possible between the Temple Hall and the Holiest of Holies. How can the rabbis explain the verse?</i>, etc.? What does Rebbi Yose do with this<sup class="footnote-marker">60</sup><i class="footnote">In this and the next sentence, the places of “R. Yose” and “the rabbis” have to be switched since the simple meaning of the verse supports R. Yose. Tosephta 2:12.</i> Between the Holiest of Holies above and the Holiest of Holies below<sup class="footnote-marker">61</sup><i class="footnote">The rabbis will dispute that even in the first Temple there was only one gobelin. Since there must be an opening for the High Priest to enter the Holiest of Holies, a complete separation so that the Holiest of Holies cannot be seen from the Temple Hall requires a minimum of two gobelins, one being closed at the place where the other is open. But on the roof of the building there was only one separating line.</i>. Do the rabbis not have this? They have it as we have stated<sup class="footnote-marker">62</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Middot</i> 4:5.</i>, “the impression of pebbles<sup class="footnote-marker">63</sup><i class="footnote">Greek ψῆφος.</i> distinguish above between holy and the Holiest of Holies.”

Halakhah 2

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> The outer one was tied open from South and the inner one from North. He walks between them until he arrives at the North end. When he arrived at the North end he turns his face to the South; he walks with his left along the gobelin<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">The Holiest of Holies being very dark, he guides his way along the inner gobelin with his left hand in which he holds the cold incense powder.</i> until he arrives at the Ark. When he came to the Ark he puts the fire-pan between the two beams<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">With which the Ark was carried (<i>Ex.</i>25:13–15). For the Second Temple, where there was no Ark, see Mishnah 3.</i>, he piles the incense on the coals and the entire House is filled with smoke. He leaves and returns in the way he entered<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">He walks backwards with his face towards the Ark inside the Holiest of Holies and towards the North between the two gobelins.</i>. He prays a short prayer<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">In the main Temple Hall.</i> but not prolonging his prayer so as not to frighten Israel<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">Who might be afraid that something had happened to him.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">64</sup><i class="footnote">Starting discussion of Mishnah 2.</i> It was stated: He enters South of the candelabrum,<sup class="footnote-marker">65</sup><i class="footnote">Which is standing at the South wall of the Sanctuary, <i>Ex.</i> 40:24, 2.5 cubits from the wall, Tosephta 2:12.</i> the words of Rebbi Meïr; Rebbi Yose says, he enters North of the Table<sup class="footnote-marker">66</sup><i class="footnote">R. Yose admits only one gobelin. The table was at the North wall, <i>Ex.</i> 40:22.</i>. Some Tannaim state, he was entering between the golden altar and the candelabrum<sup class="footnote-marker">67</sup><i class="footnote">Somewhat North of the candelabrum Tosephta 2:12, Babli 51b.</i>. He walks between them until he reaches the North. He pushes with his elbows so that the gobelins should not be burned. When he arrives at the North he turns his face to the South. He retraces his steps lest he be seen as striding between the beams. How does he do it? Rebbi Ḥanina said, he puts the bowl on the ground, throws it in the air and catches it with the fire-pan<sup class="footnote-marker">68</sup><i class="footnote">He and Samuel read the requirement that the High Priest put “his full fistfuls” of incense into the fire that in the Holiest of Holies he also has to use both his hands to put the incense in the fire, which leaves no hand free to hold the cup, forcing an acrobatic feat. Differently Babli 49b.</i>. Samuel said, he pushes it with his hands. Rebbi Joḥanan said, he empties the cup<sup class="footnote-marker">69</sup><i class="footnote">He holds that the biblical requirement is satisfied by using his fists in putting the incense into the cup. Having deposited the fire pan, the High Priest may take the cup into his right hand and empty it into the fire-pan. Opinion not mentioned in the Babli.</i> and it rises straight up, then it expands and descends.
“He leaves and returns in the way he entered.” Following Rebbi Yose, but following Rebbi Meïr, even if he wants he cannot do it. Why? Not to have his back turned to the Holiness<sup class="footnote-marker">70</sup><i class="footnote">There is no problem walking backwards according to R. Yose since he simply backs out. But for R. Meïr when he passes back between the gobelins from the North end to the middle he would turn his back towards the Ark, which is a sign of disrespect. Therefore R. Meïr should require that he back out until he is between the gobelins, then go forward until he is close to half way to the South, turn right (West) to face the Ark, and a little later make another 90° turn and walk backwards until he exits into the Temple hall.</i>.
It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">71</sup><i class="footnote"><i>2Chr.</i> 1:13. In the description of the Chronicler, the Ark was in Jerusalem in a tent erected by David but the Tent of Meeting and Bezalel’s altar were in Gibeon. Since the verse is written at the end of the description of Solomon’s visit to Gibeon, one would have expected “from the high place” מִבָּמָה (as read by LXX, most modern translators, and the Babli 53a), not “to the high place”, לַבָּמָה.</i>, <i>Solomon came to the high place in Gibeon to Jerusalem.</i> Where do we hold? If he came from Jerusalem, we should say “from Jerusalem to the high place.” If he came from the high place, we should say, “he came from the high place to Jerusalem.” Rebbi Samuel bar Eudaimon said, he came to the high place not to turn his back to the Holiness<sup class="footnote-marker">72</sup><i class="footnote">Going to Gibeon from Jerusalem he had his face always turned to face the Ark.</i>.
“He prays a short prayer.” And this was the High Priest’s prayer on the Day of Atonement when he left the Holiness in peace: “May it be the will before You, Eternal our God and God of our fathers, that there shall be no exile decreed over us, not today and not this year. But if exile was decreed over us today or this year that our exile be at a place of Torah. May it be the will before You, Eternal our God and God of our fathers, that there shall be no loss decreed over us, not today and not this year. But if loss was decreed over us today or this year that it be loss for good deeds. [May it be the will before You, Eternal our God and God of our fathers, that this year be a year of cheapness, a year of satiety, a year of trade, a year of rains, sunshine, and dew, and that your people Israel should not need one another, and do not turn to the prayer of travellers. The rabbis of Caesarea are saying, and on your people Israel that they not erect dominion one over the other.]<sup class="footnote-marker">73</sup><i class="footnote">The text in brackets is a corrector’s addition; it is from a source close to <i>Lev. rabba</i> 20(4). Since there, instead of “The rabbis of Caesarea are saying, and on your people Israel that they not erect dominion one over the other” one reads, “the rabbis of Caesarea were saying about our brothers in Caesarea, that they should not be oppressed by officials,” it seems that both the original Yerushalmi text as quite certainly the corrector’s addition (and similarly the Babli’s text in <i>Taˋanit</i> 24b) are not meant to prescribe a prayer text to the High Priest but indicate the text of the High Priest’s prayer in the re-enactment of his service in the <i>Musaf-prayer</i> of the Day of Atonement and describe the political situation in the 4<sup class="footnote-marker">th</sup> Cent. C. E..<br>The undesirable prayer of travellers is one for absence of rains in the rainy season.</i> And for the people of Sharon he was saying, may it be the will before You, Eternal our God and God of our fathers, that their houses not turn into their graves<sup class="footnote-marker">74</sup><i class="footnote">Their adobe houses are in danger of collapse during the rainy season. In <i>Lev. rabba</i> 20(4) the text reads: “The rabbis of the South (meaning of Lydda) said about our brethren in the Sharon, that their houses should not turn into their graves.” This also is from the Yerushalmi <i>Musaf</i> service.</i>”.
“He was not prolonging his prayer not to frighten Israel.” <sup class="footnote-marker">75</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 53b</i> It happened that one prolonged and they decided to enter after him<sup class="footnote-marker">76</sup><i class="footnote">To search for his corpse.</i>. One said, it was Simeon the Just. They said to him, why did you prolong? He answered them, I was praying for the Sanctuary of your God that it should not be destroyed. They said to him, nevertheless, you should not have prolonged.
<sup class="footnote-marker">77</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 39b, <i>Menaḥot</i>109b; Tosephta <i>Sotah</i> 13:8.. The first sentence is quoted in the next Chapter, 6:3.</i> Simeon the Just served Israel as High Priest for forty years, and in the last year he told them, in this year I am going to die. They asked him, from where do you know? He said to them, every year when I entered the Holiest of Holies, an old man dressed in white and his head wrapped in white entered with me and left with me. But this year he entered with me but did not leave with me. <sup class="footnote-marker">78</sup><i class="footnote">Cf Chapter 1, Notes 220 ff.</i> They asked before Rebbi Abbahu: Is it not written<sup class="footnote-marker">79</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:17.</i>, <i>nobody shall be in the Tent of Meeting during his coming to atone in the sanctuary until he leaves,</i> not even those about whom it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">80</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ez.</i> 1:10.</i>, <i>the shapes of their faces are human shapes</i> shall not be in the Tent of Meeting? He answered them, who tells me that it was a person? I am saying that it was the Holy One, praise to Him<sup class="footnote-marker">81</sup><i class="footnote">In the apparition known as <i>Shekhina.</i></i>.

Halakhah 3

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> From when the Ark was removed there was a stone there from the time of the earlier prophets; it was called Foundation, higher than the ground by three finger widths. On it he deposed it<sup class="footnote-marker">82</sup><i class="footnote">The fire pan which in Mishnah 2 was described as being put down between the beams of the Ark.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> It was stated: Before the Ark was hidden<sup class="footnote-marker">92</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 53b/54a; cf. <i>Šeqalim</i> 6:1–2.</i> he entered and exited by the light of the Ark. After the Ark was removed he was groping and entering, groping and leaving.
<sup class="footnote-marker">93</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 54b.</i> Rebbi Joḥanan said, why is it called Foundation Stone? Because on it the world is based. Rebbi Ḥiyya stated:<sup class="footnote-marker">94</sup><i class="footnote">Tosephta 2:14.</i> “Why is it called Foundation Stone? Because on it the world is based.. It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">95</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ps.</i> 50:1–2.</i>, <i>a psalm of Asaph; the power, God, the Eternal, spoke and called the earth,</i> etc., <i>from Zion, the perfection of beauty, God appears.</i> And it says<sup class="footnote-marker">96</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Is.</i> 28:16.</i>, <i>behold I founded in Zion a stone,</i> etc.”

Halakhah 4

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> He took the blood from the one who was stirring it, entered to the place where he had entered<sup class="footnote-marker">83</sup><i class="footnote">The Holiest of Holies.</i>, and stood at the place where he had stood, and sprinkled from it once upwards and seven times downwards<sup class="footnote-marker">84</sup><i class="footnote">As the verse prescribes (<i>Lev.</i> 16:14), once on the cover of the Ark and seven times in front of it.</i>. He did not intend upwards nor downwards but like one who was spanking<sup class="footnote-marker">85</sup><i class="footnote">Lifting his finger to let a drop fly off, and then dropping the finger for another drop.</i>. And so was he counting: One, one and one, one and two, one and three, one and four, one and five, one and six, one and seven. He left and put it down on the golden pedestal which was in the Temple.<br>They brought him the he-goat, he slaughtered it and received its blood in a bowl. He entered to the place where he had entered<sup class="footnote-marker">83</sup><i class="footnote">The Holiest of Holies.</i>, and stood at the place where he had stood, and sprinkled from it once upwards and seven times downwards. He did not intend downwards nor upwards but like one who was spanking. And so was he counting, etc.<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote">As detailed in Mishnah 4.</i> He left and put it down on the second pedestal which was in the Temple. Rebbi Jehudah says, only one pedestal was there.<br>He took the blood of the bull, and put down the blood of the he-goat<sup class="footnote-marker">87</sup><i class="footnote">This Mishnah follows R.
