Jehudah who insists that there was only one pedestal; therefore the bowl with the bull’s blood had to be lifted before the one with the he-goat’s blood could be deposited.</i>, and sprinkled from it on the gobelin at the place of the Ark from the outside<sup class="footnote-marker">88</sup><i class="footnote">On the gobelin in the Temple Hall, just opposite the place of the Ark in the Holiest of Holies.</i> and sprinkled from it once upwards and seven times downwards. He did not intend upwards nor downwards but like one who was spanking. And so was he counting<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote">As detailed in Mishnah 4.</i>. He took the blood of the he-goat, and put down the blood of the bull, and sprinkled from it on the gobelin at the place of the Ark from the outside and sprinkled from it once upwards and seven times downwards. He did not intend upwards nor downwards but like one who was spanking. And so was he counting<sup class="footnote-marker">86</sup><i class="footnote">As detailed in Mishnah 4.</i>. He poured the blood of the bull into the blood of the he-goat and emptied the full vessel into the empty one<sup class="footnote-marker">89</sup><i class="footnote">In order to improve the mixing of the two kinds of blood.</i>. <i>He shall go out to the altar which is before the Eternal</i><sup class="footnote-marker">90</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:18/</i><i>,</i> that is the golden altar<sup class="footnote-marker">91</sup><i class="footnote">The incense altar in the Temple Hall.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> What means כְמַצְלִיף? Rebbi Samuel bar Ḥananiah in the name of Rebbi Eleazar: Like one who whips<sup class="footnote-marker">97</sup><i class="footnote">Explanation of the Babli. <i>Arukh</i> reads כמטברר and explains “moves his hand towards the navel.”</i>.
Rebbi Joḥanan said, so he should not err<sup class="footnote-marker">98</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to the way of counting as explained in Mishnah 4. Why does he have to count 1+<i>n</i>? Babli 55a.</i>. Rebbi Zeˋira said, that he should finish his sprinkling with “seven”<sup class="footnote-marker">99</sup><i class="footnote">Since in all he has to sprinkle 8 times, it is preferable to end with “7” which is an odd number and means “luck”.</i>. But was it not stated<sup class="footnote-marker">100</sup><i class="footnote">The prefix ק is Babylonian Aramaic. The version in which the second number precedes the first is R. Jehudah’s in Tosephta 2:14, R. Meïr’s in the Babli 55a.</i>, “seven and one”? Rebbi Abun said, it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">101</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:14; cf. Note 84.</i>, <i>before the cover .. seven.</i> Why does the verse say, <i>he shall sprinkle?</i> That the first sprinkling should be counted with them<sup class="footnote-marker">102</sup><i class="footnote">Sprinkling is mentioned separately for the blood on the cover of the Ark and the seven times in front of the Ark. Therefore they have to be mentioned separately in counting. Babli 55a.</i>.
It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">103</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:15, about the blood of the he-goat.</i>, <i>he shall sprinkle it on the cover.</i> I could think on its top, the verse says, <i>in front of the cover.</i> I could think on its front, the verse says, <i>on, in front of</i><sup class="footnote-marker">104</sup><i class="footnote">Therefore the blood of the he-goat must be sprinkled both on and in front of the cover. No numbers are indicated.</i>. Rebbi Zeˋira said, it needs to touch; Rebbi Samuel bar Rav Isaac said, it does not need to touch. Rebbi Abun bar Ḥiyya said, the reason of Rebbi Samuel bar Rav Isaac: <i>he shall sprinkle it on the cover and in front of the cover.</i> Since “the cover” mentioned there<sup class="footnote-marker">105</sup><i class="footnote">About the bull, where it is spelled out (v. 14) that the High Priest with his finger sprinkles <i>to the East towards the front of the cover</i> and <i>seven times in front of the cover.</i></i> means in front of but not on its top and it does not need to touch, also “the cover” mentioned here<sup class="footnote-marker">106</sup><i class="footnote">About the he-goat’s blood (v. 15).</i> means in front of but not on its top and it does not need to touch. Rebbi Yose said, Rebbi Abun bar Ḥiyya thinks that the upwards sprinkling of the he-goat is inferred from the upwards sprinkling of the bull, but it is not so, but the upwards sprinkling of the he-goat is inferred from the downwards sprinkling of the bull<sup class="footnote-marker">107</sup><i class="footnote">Therefore the disagreement between R. Zeˋira and R. Samuel bar Rav Isaac remains open.</i>:
<sup class="footnote-marker">108</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Sifra Aḥare Parashah</i> 3(3–7), Babli 55a.</i><i>“He shall sprinkle it</i><sup class="footnote-marker">103</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:15, about the blood of the he-goat.</i><i>, [in front of the</i> <i>cover</i>]<sup class="footnote-marker">109</sup><i class="footnote">Unjustified addition by the corrector.</i>, this teaches that he gives a single one upwards<sup class="footnote-marker">110</sup><i class="footnote">The singular “it” implies a single sprinkling.</i>. <i>In front of the cover,</i> I do not know how many<sup class="footnote-marker">111</sup><i class="footnote">No numbers are mentioned in <i>Lev.</i> 16:15.</i>. So I am arguing: It mentions giving the bull’s blood downwards, and it mentions giving the he-goat’s blood downwards. Since giving the bull’s blood downwards as mentioned is seven times<sup class="footnote-marker">112</sup><i class="footnote">Explicit in <i>Lev.</i> 16:14.</i>, so giving the he-goat’s blood downwards as mentioned must be seven times. Or go in the following way: Blood is mentioned upwards and blood is mentioned downwards. Since the blood mentioned upwards is once, so the blood mentioned downwards must be once. Let us see to what it is comparable. One argues downwards from downwards; one does not argue downwards from upwards. Or go in the following way: One argues he-goat’s blood from he-goat’s blood; but one does not argue he-goat’s blood from bull’s blood. The verse says, <i>he shall treat its blood as he treated the bull’s blood.</i> Since the bull’s blood is downwards seven times, also the he-goat’s blood is downwards seven times. But I do not know how many times to give the bull’s blood upwards. Giving the blood upwards is mentioned for the he-goat and giving the blood upwards is mentioned for the bull. Since giving the blood upwards as mentioned for the he-goat is once, so giving the blood upwards as mentioned for the bull is once. Or go in the following way: Blood is mentioned downwards; blood is mentioned upwards. Since the blood mentioned downwards is seven, so the blood mentioned upwards must be seven. Let us see to what it is similar. One argues upwards from upwards; one does not argue upwards from downwards. Or go in the following way: One argues bull’s blood from bull’s blood; but one does not argue bull’s blood from he-goat’s blood. The verse says, <i>he shall treat its blood as he treated the bull’s blood,</i> that all its works be the same. Since the bull’s blood is seven times downwards, also the he-goat’s blood is seven times downwards. Since the he-goat’s blood is once upwards, also the bull’s blood is once upwards<sup class="footnote-marker">113</sup><i class="footnote">The number of sprinklings are uniquely determined, upwards by inference from v. 15, downwards explicitly in v.14.</i>.”
<i>The holiness</i><sup class="footnote-marker">114</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:16.</i><i>.</i> He has to aim vis-a-vis the holiness<sup class="footnote-marker">115</sup><i class="footnote">This explains the statement of Mishnah 6 that blood sprinkled on the gobelin in the Temple Hall must be applied at the spot in front of the Ark.</i>. <sup class="footnote-marker">116</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Sifra Aḥare Pereq</i> 3(7–8). Babli 59b.</i>“Rebbi Nehemiah said, since we find about the bull which comes for all commandments<sup class="footnote-marker">117</sup><i class="footnote">This is the expression of the verse (<i>Lev.</i> 4:2) to describe the purification offerings required for an anointed High Priest and the High Court; cf. Introduction to Tractate <i>Horaiot.</i></i> that he stands before the altar and sprinkles on the gobelin at the moment of his sprinkling<sup class="footnote-marker">118</sup><i class="footnote">Since the High Priest is commanded to bring the blood into the Sanctuary (<i>Lev.</i>4:5), to sprinkle from it seven times on the gobelin (v.6), and without moving give blood on the four corners of the incense altar (v.7), it is clear that he has to stand in front of the altar and sprinkle the blood long distance in the direction of the gobelin.</i>, I could think that here it is the same; the verse says<sup class="footnote-marker">119</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:18: <i>He shall exit to the altar which is before the Eternal.</i></i>, <i>which is before the Eternal.</i> Where was he<sup class="footnote-marker">120</sup><i class="footnote">Coming from the Holiest of Holies the High Priest stands between the gobelin and the altar.</i>? Inside of the altar. Or does he speak only of the outer altar? The verse says, <i>which is before the Eternal.</i> Therefore he only speaks of the inner altar<sup class="footnote-marker">121</sup><i class="footnote">Which is standing in the Temple hall directly opposite the ark in the Holiest of Holies.</i>.”
Everybody agrees about the bull of the anointed and the community that it need not touch<sup class="footnote-marker">122</sup><i class="footnote">Since the High Priest is standing too far away from the gobelin.</i>. Where do they disagree? About the bull and the he-goat of the day of Atonement. There are Tannaim who state, it needs to touch. There are Tannaim: it does not need to touch<sup class="footnote-marker">123</sup><i class="footnote">The disagreement between R. Zeˋira and R. Samuel bar Rav Isaac is a much older controversy.</i>. Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Yose said, I saw it in Rome<sup class="footnote-marker">124</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 37a; cf. 4:1 Note 40. Tosephta 2:14.</i> full of drops of blood. I said, these are of the blood sprinkled on it on the Day of Atonement. This implies that it needs to touch. [Even if you say that it does not need to touch]<sup class="footnote-marker">125</sup><i class="footnote">Addition by the corrector; the argument could be implied by the scribe’s text. The form תימא, derived from the Accadic/Babylonian Aramaic root אמא “to speak”, is impossible in a Yerushalmi text.</i>, (but)<sup class="footnote-marker">126</sup><i class="footnote">Scribe’s text.</i> if it touched, it touched.
If one gave from a sanctified vessel<sup class="footnote-marker">127</sup><i class="footnote">A vessel dedicated to the Temple service.</i> to a profane vessel he disqualified<sup class="footnote-marker">128</sup><i class="footnote">The disqualification is not absolute since Mishnah <i>Zevaḥim</i> 3:2 states that the blood will be qualified if returned to a sanctified vessel. The Babli has another reading of the question, 58a.</i>. Does this imply that from a sanctified vessel to a sanctified vessel it remains qualified<sup class="footnote-marker">129</sup><i class="footnote">This question is asked not for the day of Atonement but for all year round. Does blood received in a sanctified vessel have to be brought to the altar in this vessel or not?</i>? Rebbi Haggai said before Rebbi Yose, the Mishnah implies this: “He poured the blood of the bull into the blood of the he-goat. Rebbi Mana said, could we say, the blood of the bull from a full vessel into the blood of the he-goat in an empty vessel<sup class="footnote-marker">130</sup><i class="footnote">The Mishnah does not prove anything since the second vessel is not empty; the second vessel is not a replacement of the first.</i>? Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, he poured the blood of the bull from a full vessel into the blood of the he-goat in a full vessel; after that he again mixes them into another vessel<sup class="footnote-marker">131</sup><i class="footnote">Which in the Mishnah is the original vessel of the bull’s blood, but for the mixture it is a new vessel. Therefore in this case one is required to pour blood from the original sanctified vessel into another sanctified vessel. This proves R. Haggai’s point.</i> to make a perfect mixture.
From where that he is required to pour out<sup class="footnote-marker">132</sup><i class="footnote">Why must the blood of the bull and the blood of the he-goat be mixed before given on the corners of the golden altar; Mishnah 6. The Babli does not necessarily accept the Mishnah, 57b–58a.</i>? The verse says<sup class="footnote-marker">133</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:18, misquoted.</i>, <i>he shall give of the blood of the bull and the blood of the he-goat,</i> when they are mixed. I could think each one by itself, the verse says<sup class="footnote-marker">134</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ex.</i> 30:10.</i>, <i>Aaron shall atone on its corners once yearly,</i> he atones once yearly, he does not atone twice yearly<sup class="footnote-marker">135</sup><i class="footnote">Not even one directly after the other.</i>. Or should we say, the bull’s blood once yearly, not twice yearly? Rebbi Ismael stated, <i>from the blood of the atoning purification offering</i><sup class="footnote-marker">134</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ex.</i> 30:10.</i><i>,</i> he atones once yearly, he does not atone twice yearly. Everybody agrees that for the seven sprinklings downward<sup class="footnote-marker">136</sup><i class="footnote">Regarding the incense altar, it is required by <i>Lev.</i> 16:19 that the High Priest sprinkle on its top “seven times of the blood.” Since no mention is made of bull or he-goat, the verse must refer to the mixed blood. <i>Sifra Aḥare Pereq</i> 4(8).</i> he has to pour<sup class="footnote-marker">137</sup><i class="footnote">I. e., to mix.</i>, for it is written <i>seven,</i> not fourteen.
If he received of the bull’s blood in three cups and of the he-goat’s blood in three cups, to give from one between the beams, from one on the gobelins, from one on the golden altar. Which of them is he obligated to pour<sup class="footnote-marker">138</sup><i class="footnote">To mix for sprinkling on the top of the golden altar. It is obvious that the discussion here presupposes that there be no mixing for giving the blood on the corners of the golden altar; otherwise there would be only two cups possible.</i>? May a person think of half an atonement<sup class="footnote-marker">139</sup><i class="footnote">Since the he-goat was made a purification sacrifice (Chapter 4 Note 5) and is disqualified if the blood was not received with the appropriate intention (Mishnah <i>Zevaḥim</i> 1:1), the blood must be received with the intent to be used for full atonement. The objection contradicts the anonymous Tanna in Mishnah 9, for whom all actions of the day separate atonements. As seen from the next section, the objection and the reformulation can be disregarded.</i>? But it is so: If he received of the bull’s blood in three cups [and of the he-goat’s blood in three cups,]<sup class="footnote-marker">140</sup><i class="footnote">Addition of the corrector which must be deleted following the argument of the preceding Note.</i> to give from one between the beams, and from one on the gobelins, and from one on the golden altar. Which of them is he obligated to pour? It is a disagreement between Rebbi Zeˋira and Rebbi Hila, since they disagreed:
<sup class="footnote-marker">141</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph is repeated in Halakhah 6:1 (6).</i> If he drew lots for three pairs<sup class="footnote-marker">142</sup><i class="footnote">Instead of one pair of he-goats there were three; for each group of sprinkling one was slaughtered while the other was alive.</i>, to give from one between the beams, from one on the gobelins, from one on the golden altar. Which of them is sent away? Rebbi Zeˋira said, <i>to atone on him</i><sup class="footnote-marker">143</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:10.</i><i>,</i> one with whom one atones, the companion is sent away; one with whom one does not atone, the companion is not sent away.. Rebbi Hila said, <i>to atone on him,</i> one with whom one completes atonement, the companion is sent away, one with whom one does not complete atonement, the companion is not sent away. In Rebbi Zeˋira’s opinion, all three are sent away. In Rebbi Hila’s opinion, only the last one is sent away.
And here, in Rebbi Zeˋira’s opinion, he must pour all three; in Rebbi Hila’s opinion, he must pour only the one from which he sprinkled<sup class="footnote-marker">144</sup><i class="footnote">On the corners of the altar.</i>.
If he received of the bull’s blood in three cups and of the he-goat’s blood in three cups, to give from one between the beams, from one on the gobelins, from one on the golden altar. Which of them is poured into the base<sup class="footnote-marker">145</sup><i class="footnote">While it is not mentioned in <i>Lev.</i> 16, it is understood from <i>Lev.</i> 4 that the blood remaining after some of it was sprinkled on the four corners of the large altar is poured onto the base of the altar (<i>Lev</i>.4:25,30,34). The same is done with the blood of the bull of the anointed and the community (<i>Lev</i>.4:7, 18) and therefore also applies to the purification offerings of the Day of Atonement.</i>? The disagreement between Rebbi and Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Simeon, as they disagreed: <sup class="footnote-marker">146</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Sifra Wayyiqra II (Ḥovah) Pereq</i>10(4–6), Babli 57b, <i>Zevaḥim</i> 34b.</i>“A purification offering whose blood was received in four cups and from each one he gave one giving<sup class="footnote-marker">147</sup><i class="footnote">The “giving” is sprinkling of blood on one corner of the large altar.</i>, from where that all of them are poured on the base? The verse says<sup class="footnote-marker">148</sup><i class="footnote">A misquote from <i>Lev</i>.4:25 (it should be דָּמוֹ not דָּמָהּ. All quotes from v. 25 should be replaced by v. 30,34 and vice-versa.</i>, <i>and its blood he shall pour.</i> I could think that if he {only}<sup class="footnote-marker">149</sup><i class="footnote">Word missing in the text, added from the parallels and needed for logical consistency.</i> gave all four givings from one of them, all of them should be poured, the verse says,<sup class="footnote-marker">150</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev</i>.4:30,34. See Note 148.</i> <i>and all its blood he shall pour.</i> How is this? It is poured on the base, and they are emptied into the canal<sup class="footnote-marker">151</sup><i class="footnote">The water supply to the Temple which emptied into the Siloam pool.</i>, the words of Rebbi. Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Simeon: From where that even if he gave all four givings from one of them, all of them shall be poured on the base? The verse says, <i>and its blood he shall pour.</i> In Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Simeon’s opinion, all are poured into the base. In Rebbi’s opinion, only the one from which he sprinkled is poured<sup class="footnote-marker">152</sup><i class="footnote">In Rebbi’s opinion, only the actual use of blood in a vessel qualifies the remainder to be poured on the base of the altar; in R. Eleazar ben R. Simeon’s opinion, all eligible blood in a Temple vessel which is not disqualified is qualified to be poured on the base.</i>.
The colleagues say<sup class="footnote-marker">153</sup><i class="footnote">They have a tradition that Rebbi disagrees also if the blood of two purification offerings were mixed together in one vessel.</i>, if one becomes <i>piggul</i><sup class="footnote-marker">154</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Piggul</i> is consumption of sacrifices out of their allotted time (<i>Lev.</i> 19::7) our out of the proper place. Since a sacrifice cannot become disqualified retroactively, the technical term <i>piggul</i> is used to describe the disqualification caused by the intent of future <i>piggul</i> in any of the required actions in processing the sacrifice (slaughter, reception of the blood, bringing to the altar, sprinkling on the corners). Processing <i>piggul</i> sacrifice is sinful; therefore blood containing <i>piggul</i> blood cannot be used; it is disqualified.</i><i>,</i> so does the other; if the parts<sup class="footnote-marker">155</sup><i class="footnote">The fat which is forbidden for human consumption, cf. Chapter 5:2, Note 50.</i> of one were lost, one sprinkles for the parts of the other. Everybody agrees about the bull of the Anointed or the community<sup class="footnote-marker">122</sup><i class="footnote">Since the High Priest is standing too far away from the gobelin.</i>, unless there be one giving of each of them. The colleagues say, qualified parts which were mixed up with disqualified parts, only if there was a giving<sup class="footnote-marker">147</sup><i class="footnote">The “giving” is sprinkling of blood on one corner of the large altar.</i> of the qualified. Where do they disagree? About the blood of two purification sacrifices which were mixed up. <sup class="footnote-marker">156</sup><i class="footnote">Babli <i>Zevaḥim</i> 95a.</i> Rebbi says, I am saying one investigates the blood; if there is enough for one giving for each one it is qualified, otherwise it is disqualified. But the Sages say, even if there is only one giving [for both of them]<sup class="footnote-marker">157</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition.</i> it is qualified. In Rebbi’s opinion, there is a measure for givings, in the Sages’ opinion there is no measure for givings<sup class="footnote-marker">158</sup><i class="footnote">If Rebbi requires visibly enough blood for two givings, he must require more than a tiny drop for each giving. This amount is not spelled out anywhere. For the Sages a tiny drop is enough and this is available in any mixture, even if not recognizable separately.</i>. This implies<sup class="footnote-marker">159</sup><i class="footnote">For the Sages, whom practice has to follow, two separate purification offerings whose blood has been mixed are treated as one body.</i>, if one becomes <i>piggul,</i> so does the other; if the parts of one were lost, one sprinkles for the parts of the other.

Halakhah 5

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> He<sup class="footnote-marker">160</sup><i class="footnote">The High Priest, exiting from the Holiest of Holies, standing at the Southwest corner of the Temple Hall with his face to the West. As the Halakhah explains, he has to continue walking backwards with his face to the West until he stays East of the golden altar; then he turns right to the Northeast corner of the golden altar.</i> started purifying<sup class="footnote-marker">161</sup><i class="footnote">This meaning of the root חטא is derived from <i>Lev.</i> 14:49. Here it means sprinkling blood on the four corners of the golden altar.</i> and moves. Where does he start? At the Northeast corner<sup class="footnote-marker">162</sup><i class="footnote">If the High Priest stands in front of the altar, the NE corner is the first corner to his right, and there he starts since there is a rule that all voluntary turns in the Temple have to be to the right, the lucky side.</i>, Northwest, Southwest, Southeast. At the place where he starts purifyng on the outer altar<sup class="footnote-marker">163</sup><i class="footnote">There is a walkway around the large outer altar at half height. Since this altar is accessed by the ramp on its South side, if the Cohen turns to his right entering the walkway, the first corner he arrives at is the SE corner. (On the walkway he naturally has to make 4 left turns, but these are forced by his original right turn.)</i>, there he finishes on the inner altar. Rebbi Eliezer says, he was standing on his place and purifying<sup class="footnote-marker">164</sup><i class="footnote">If he stands in front of the altar to the South, he might go straight ahead to the SE corner, but if it is required that he start with a right turn by necessity he comes to the NE corner.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Should he not start at the Southeast corner? Rebbi Hila said, right turn. This is no right turn<sup class="footnote-marker">164</sup><i class="footnote">If he stands in front of the altar to the South, he might go straight ahead to the SE corner, but if it is required that he start with a right turn by necessity he comes to the NE corner.</i>. Should he not start at the Northwest corner? Rebbi Eleazar said, <i>he shall leave to the altar</i><sup class="footnote-marker">165</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:18. This is read to require that he stand in front of the altar before starting the sprinkling. Therefore he has to start to the East.</i><i>.</i> Should he not start at the Southwest corner? Not to turn his back on the Holiness<sup class="footnote-marker">166</sup><i class="footnote">Leaving the gobelins he stands in the SW between gobelin and altar. To start at the SW corner, he has to turn around.</i>. Does he not end to turn his back on the Holiness? He was returning backwards<sup class="footnote-marker">167</sup><i class="footnote">If he starts at the NE corner, in the end he has to go from the SW to the SE corners turning his back to the Ark. Therefore he has to walk this stretch backwards, facing W. The rule of the Mishnah is the only one compatible with all constraints.</i>. He shall stand in the South and start at the Northeast corner, as Rebbi Hila said, right turn. This is no right turn.
It was stated:<sup class="footnote-marker">168</sup><i class="footnote">Tosephta 3:1, <i>Sifra Aḥare Pereq</i> 4(10), Babli 59a. The text here seems to be the correct one, against the three witnesses to the Babylonian text.</i> Rebbi Eliezer says, he was standing at his place and purifying. On all of them he was giving from top to bottom except for the one he was standing in front of [in the diagonal]<sup class="footnote-marker">169</sup><i class="footnote">Addition of the corrector from the Tosephta. Greek λοξόν, “oblique”.</i>, where he was giving from bottom to top<sup class="footnote-marker">170</sup><i class="footnote">Since the top of the golden altar was only 1 cubit square, it was easily possible to sprinkle on all horns when standing in front of one corner.</i>. Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: Both of them were explaining the same verse<sup class="footnote-marker">171</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:18. The blood must be sprinkled around; the way of delivery is not indicated.</i>, <i>around.</i> [The rabbis are saying, around walking. Rebbi Eliezer is saying, around]<sup class="footnote-marker">171</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:18. The blood must be sprinkled around; the way of delivery is not indicated.</i> the corners.
Two Cohanim escaped the wars<sup class="footnote-marker">172</sup><i class="footnote">Greek πόλεμος, ὁ “war”; in this case the first war against the Romans. Babli 59a.</i>. One said, I was standing and purifying; the other one said, I was walking and purifying. Rebbi Yudan said, this implies, he who does it one way does not worry, and he who does it the other way does not worry<sup class="footnote-marker">173</sup><i class="footnote">Disregarding both Talmudim, Maimonides rules against R. Eliezer both in his Mishnah commentary and in his Code.</i>.

Halakhah 6

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> On all of them he gives from bottom to top except the one he is standing in front of, where he gives from top to bottom<sup class="footnote-marker">174</sup><i class="footnote">This follows R. Eliezer. If he would give the blood with his finger on the horn directly in front of him from bottom to top, some blood would flow back onto his arm and dirty his white robe.</i>. He sprinkles on the surface of the altar seven times<sup class="footnote-marker">175</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:19.</i>. The rest of the blood he poured on the Western base of the outer altar<sup class="footnote-marker">176</sup><i class="footnote">While this is not prescribed in <i>Lev.</i> 16, as explained in the Halakhah it is inferred from the treatment of the blood of the bull of the Anointed Priest, whose remainders have to be poured on the “base of the altar which is in front of the Tent of Meeting.” “In front of” is taken to refer to “base”, this is the Western side of the base of the altar.</i>; those of the outer altar one pours on the southern base. This and that combine in the water canal<sup class="footnote-marker">151</sup><i class="footnote">The water supply to the Temple which emptied into the Siloam pool.</i> and leave towards the Kidron valley where it is sold to gardeners as fertilizer; one commits larceny with it<sup class="footnote-marker">177</sup><i class="footnote">The water coming out of the Temple is made to drip into the earth, where the blood is absorbed, and at the bottom clear water is reappearing. The earth enriched with the blood is sold to vegetable growers as fertilizer. Since this was part of the construction of the Temple, the Temple does not renounce proprietorship of the blood suspended in the water; therefore use of the enriched earth without paying redemption money to the Temple is stealing from Heaven’s property.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <i>He shall sprinkle on it</i><sup class="footnote-marker">178</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:19.</i><i>,</i> not on its ashes. <i>On it,</i> not on its coals<sup class="footnote-marker">179</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 59a, Tosephta 3:2.</i>. There are Tannaim who state, the North side. There are Tannaim who state, the South side. He who says, the North side, Rebbi Eliezer; he who says the South side, the rabbis<sup class="footnote-marker">180</sup><i class="footnote">Since for R. Eliezer the High Priest always stands at the NE corner of the golden altar. For the rabbis, he finishes giving the blood on the corners at the SE corner, when he starts to sprinkle the top seven times.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">181</sup><i class="footnote">Tosephta 3:7, <i>Sifra Aḥare Pereq</i> 3(7); <i>Zevaḥim</i> 58b. The text of the second sentence is the scribe’s, the one in brackets the corrector’s. Since the two sentences of the scribe are essentially identical, the corrector’s text should be accepted (even though the parallel sources show that it would have been better to correct the second sentence.)</i>“Rebbi Yose said, this is a memorandum: Anything taken from inside to be given outside is given to what is close to the inside. [Anything taken from the outside to be given inside is taken from what is close to the inside.] And all that comes out from the inside to be given outside is given from what is close to the inside<sup class="footnote-marker">182</sup><i class="footnote">Anything taken from inside, the remainder of blood used on the Day of Atonement or of the bull of the Anointed or of the commonwealth, outside has to be given close to the inside, i. e., on the Western base of the altar. Similarly, the incense taken from the table with the shew-bread to be burned on the outside altar has to be burned on the Western side of the altar. And anything taken from the outside to be taken inside, coals for the incense altar and fire to light the candelabrum, have to be taken from the Western side of the outside altar close to the Temple entrance.</i>.”
Rebbi Jeremiah in the name of Rebbi Pedat. The coals of every day and the Western light<sup class="footnote-marker">183</sup><i class="footnote">On the candelabrum.</i> are inferred from the Day of Atonement. And the two censers are inferred from the remainder blood<sup class="footnote-marker">184</sup><i class="footnote">As explained in Note 182.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">185</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Sifra Wayyiqra II (Ḥovah) Parashah</i> 3(12); Babli 52a.</i>“<i>And all blood of the bull he shall pour</i><sup class="footnote-marker">186</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev</i>. 4:7.</i><i>,</i> to include the blood of the bull of the Day of Atonement in pouring.” And why did he not say, “and the he-goat”? Rebbi Mana said, is it not required to be mixed<sup class="footnote-marker">187</sup><i class="footnote">If the bull’s blood has to be poured on the base of the large altar, the pouring of the he-goat’s blood is an automatic consequence and does not have to be spelled out as a separate commandment. Cf. Chapter 1, Note 200.</i>? You conclude in saying, <i>and all blood of the bull he shall pour,</i> to include the blood of the bull and the he-goat of the Day of Atonement in pouring.
<i>When he finished atoning the sanctuary</i><sup class="footnote-marker">188</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:20.</i><i>.</i> There are Tannaim who state, when he finished, he atoned<sup class="footnote-marker">189</sup><i class="footnote">If he correctly finished the ceremonies, automatically he atoned. Cf. Babli 60b.</i> There are Tannaim who state, when he atoned, he finished<sup class="footnote-marker">190</sup><i class="footnote">Only if he did everything required for atoning he is finished.</i>. Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: They differ by disagreement. He who said, when he atoned, he finished, the remainder is obstructive<sup class="footnote-marker">191</sup><i class="footnote">If the remaining blood is not poured on the Western base of the exterior altar, the interior ceremonies are invalid. Babli, <i>Zevaḥim</i> 111a.</i>. He who said, when he finished, he atoned, the remainder is not obstructive. Rebbi Joshua ben Levi said, they differ in understanding. About the remainder (is it obstructive?), the remainder is not obstructive. Rebbi Simon in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi, the remainder is not obstructive. How is this? He who said, when he finished, he atoned, makes it four givings<sup class="footnote-marker">192</sup><i class="footnote">There are four ceremonies: Blood in the Holiest of Holies, on the gobelins, on the corners of the interior altar, and on its top. If one of them is invalid, it has to be repeated.</i>. He who said, when he atoned, he finished, makes it only one giving<sup class="footnote-marker">193</sup><i class="footnote">If part is invalid, the entire ceremony has to be repeated from the start.</i>.
It was stated: <sup class="footnote-marker">194</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Sifra Wayyiqra II (Ḥovah) Pereq</i> 9(2); cf. Basbli 52a.</i>“Rebbi Ismael said, if the remainder blood of purification sacrifices which does not atone<sup class="footnote-marker">195</sup><i class="footnote">The blood on the corners of the altar atones. In general if the blood becomes disqualified after this the purification sacrifice remains qualified. The only problem is the status of blood which was brought into the Sanctuary.</i> is given on the base, the start of an elevation sacrifice which is atoning<sup class="footnote-marker">196</sup><i class="footnote">The blood of the elevation sacrifice which, in contrast to the purification sacrifice, is not given on the four horns of the altar at the corners but only on the lower walls of two diagonally opposed corners so that blood is splattered on all four walls of the altar.. The question is, which pair of corners, SW and NE, or NW and SE? While the elevation offering is voluntary, it is stated in <i>Lev</i>. 1:4 that it is atoning. While the verse does not detail for what it is atoning, it is concluded in <i>Sifra Wayyiqra I Pereq</i> 4(8) that it is for the transgressions which do not qualify for a purification offering, infraction of positive commandments and of minor prohibitions. The“start” is giving the blood on the walls of the altar.</i> it is only logical that it be given on the base<sup class="footnote-marker">197</sup><i class="footnote">The SE corner of the altar had no base stones standing out from the walls of the altar. The argument shows that the blood of the elevation sacrifice has to be applied to the SW and NE corners. (Mishnah <i>Tamid</i>4:1).</i>. Rebbi Aqiba said to him, No. If you said that the remainder blood of purification sacrifices which does not atone and is not able to atone are given on the base, the start of an elevation sacrifice which is atoning and is able to atone is only logical that it be given on the base.” He who said “does not atone”, they do not atone during all other days of the year; therefore on the Day of Atonement they atone<sup class="footnote-marker">198</sup><i class="footnote">Since the ritual of the Day of Atonement in <i>Lev</i>. 16:29 is called <i>an eternal law</i>, any particular action required is essential for Atonement. But an action is certainly obstructive only if it is mentioned in Chapter 16.</i>. He who says “does not atone and is not able to atone”, they do not atone either on New Year’s Day<sup class="footnote-marker">198a</sup><i class="footnote">“On New Year’s Day” may be a scribal error for כָּל־יְמוֹת הַשָּׁנָה “all days of the year.”</i> and not on the Day of Atonement. Where do we hold? If for a commandment, it is a commandment to give on the base. But if it cannot refer to the commandment, let it refer to obstruction<sup class="footnote-marker">199</sup><i class="footnote">Since it was established earlier (Note 185) that it is a commandment to pour the remaining blood on the base, the difference between R. Ismael and R. Aqiba can only be whether pouring the blood on the base is obstructive or not.</i>.
Rebbi Shammai said, a <i>baraita</i> implies that the remainders are obstructive, as we have stated: <sup class="footnote-marker">200</sup><i class="footnote">Babli <i>Zevaḥim</i> 52b, <i>Sifra Ṣaw Pereq</i> 3(4).</i>“The lower ones, if given on the upper did not placate since nothing of them is brought on the upper, should you not say about the upper ones, if given on the lower they placate since something of them is brought below<sup class="footnote-marker">201</sup><i class="footnote">Blood of elevation and well-being sacrifices which has to be given on the walls of the altar below the walkway at half-height certainly cannot validly be given on the upper part of the walls, but blood of purification sacrifices which must be given on the horns of the altar (by a Cohen standing on the walkway) should be valid if given on the lower walls since at the end the remainder of the blood is poured on the base which is below the lower walls.</i>? The inner ones<sup class="footnote-marker">202</sup><i class="footnote">Blood used inside the Sanctuary, of the day of Atonement, and of the bulls of the Anointed and the community.</i> shall prove, since some of them is given outside, but if he gave them outside<sup class="footnote-marker">203</sup><i class="footnote">If none of the blood was brought inside, the ceremony certainly is invalid.</i> it did not placate, since the altar did not cleanse them<sup class="footnote-marker">204</sup><i class="footnote">Since the altar is the place of only the third and fourths stops in the use of the blood inside the Sanctuary.</i>, what should you say about the upper ones, if given on the lower they should placate since the horns cleanse them<sup class="footnote-marker">205</sup><i class="footnote">After blood of purification sacrifices was given on the horns, what is left becomes remainder.</i>. Since the horns cleanse them, if he gave them below it should be qualified. The verse says <i>it</i><sup class="footnote-marker">206</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev</i>. 6:19. The purification sacrifice except for the parts destined for the altar is eaten by the Cohanim, but only if the priest <i>purified it</i>, i. e., followed all the prescribed rules.</i>, that he give the blood on the upper, but not that he give in the lower.” What does it mean, “the altar did not cleanse them”? Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, it does not cleanse them to turn them into remainders; only through the beams and the gobelins<sup class="footnote-marker">207</sup><i class="footnote">Blood on the altar is invalid if from it was not previously given between the beams and on the gobelins.</i> they become remainders.
Rebbi Yose said, a Mishnah implies that the remainders are not obstructive, as we have stated:<sup class="footnote-marker">208</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Zevaḥim</i> 5:1, speaking of the remainders of the blood brought inside.</i> “If he did not give, it does not obstruct.” Rebbi Borqai in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: a <i>baraita</i> implies that remainders are obstructive, as we have stated: <sup class="footnote-marker">209</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Sifra Aḥare Pereq</i> 8(8) on <i>Lev</i>. 16:29; Babli 61a.</i>“<i>He shall atone for the holy Sanctuary</i>, that is the innermost room, <i>and the tent of Meeting</i>, this is the Temple Hall, <i>and the altar</i>, this is the [golden]<sup class="footnote-marker">210</sup><i class="footnote">Addition by the corrector; a correct statement but unnecessary as shown by the parallels.</i> altar, <i>he shall atone</i>, also for the courtyards.” What atonement do you have for the courtyards? Not the remainders<sup class="footnote-marker">211</sup><i class="footnote">And anything needed for atonement is obstructive.</i>? [Rebbi Abun bar Ḥiyya asked, according to him who said that]<sup class="footnote-marker">212</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition.</i> remainders are obstructive, is their place obstructive<sup class="footnote-marker">213</sup><i class="footnote">It seems that here are two different texts. The scribe’s text is “Are not the remainders obstructive? Their place is obstructive.” After having proved that the <i>baraita</i> presupposes that remainders are obstructive it is stated that if the remainders of blood brought into the sanctuary are not given on the base to the West of the exterior altar, the procedure is invalid. In the corrector’s text this is a question, not an assertion.</i>? If he gave them in the night, does he have to slaughter a new sacrifice for them<sup class="footnote-marker">214</sup><i class="footnote">No necessary action in the Temple can be performed in the night; only leftovers from the preceding day are burned on the altar. Pouring remainders of blood on the base in the night clearly is invalid; the question is whether this requires a new sacrifice. The question cannot be asked about the service of the Day of Atonement, it must be about the bull of the Anointed or the community.</i>? The colleagues asked: Does one think about them<sup class="footnote-marker">215</sup><i class="footnote">Since it is agreed that pouring the remainder blood on the base in a commandment, if a sacrifice is slaughtered with the intent not to pour, or the blood is brought to the alter with the intent not to pour the remainder on the base, is the sacrifice disqualified from the moment of the illegitimate thought? Answered in the affirmative in the Babli, <i>Zevaḥim</i> 29a.</i>? Rebbi Yudan asked: if they are lost? What is problematic for him, if he started and they became deficient. But if he did not start to give everybody agrees that what he leaves over are leftovers<sup class="footnote-marker">216</sup><i class="footnote">The commandment to pour the remainders on the base is conditional; if there are no remainders, there is no obligation to pour.</i>.
It was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">217</sup><i class="footnote">Tosephta <i>Zevaḥim</i> 6:9; Babli <i>Yoma</i>59a, <i>Meˋilah</i> 11a.</i>: “One commits larceny with blood<sup class="footnote-marker">218</sup><i class="footnote">Illegitimate use of <i>sancta</i> is larceny which requires restitution, payment of a fine, and a sacrifice (<i>Lev</i>. 5:14–16). The question is whether this applies also to the blood when it flows out of the Temple domain after all ceremonies have successfully been completed.</i>, the words of Rebbi Meïr and Rebbi Simeon, but the Sages are saying, there is no larceny with blood.” Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan, <i>for the blood is it, it atones for the person</i><sup class="footnote-marker">219</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev</i>. 17:11.</i>. You only have atonement of persons from it. Rebbi Ḥiyya in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan, <i>any who eats it will be extirpated</i><sup class="footnote-marker">220</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev</i>. 17:14.</i>. You only have extirpation of persons from it<sup class="footnote-marker">221</sup><i class="footnote">In both cases, the argument is that after the blood has left the Temple precinct it is profane. It still may be Temple property, but no sacrilege is involved in unauthorized use and no sacrifice for <i>meˋilah</i> can be due.</i>. Rebbi Zeˋira said, they differ if he dedicated blood<sup class="footnote-marker">222</sup><i class="footnote">It is not clear what this means. It could be that one refers to blood of sacrifices which somehow became disqualified for the altar, or of the blood of animals unfit for the altar which from the start were donated only for the upkeep of the Temple, and whose illicit use is <i>meˋilah</i>.</i>. He who said, you only have atonement of persons from it, and this since there is no atonement from it there is no larceny with it. He who says, you only have extirpation of persons from it, and since there is extirpation from it there is larceny with it<sup class="footnote-marker">223</sup><i class="footnote">Both possibilities apply to both interpretations given in the preceding Note.</i>. There came Rebbi Abba, Rebbi Ḥiyya in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan, they differ if he dedicated blood or for the upkeep of the Temple. Rebbi Zeˋira enjoyed it; he thought that it had been said about the rabbis. He said to him, what do you have in your hand? It was said about Rebbi Simeon<sup class="footnote-marker">224</sup><i class="footnote">R. Simeon holds that the remainders of blood used on the altar, as the blood mentioned in Mishnah 8, as well as the blood of animals dedicated to the upkeep of the Temple, are subject to <i>meˋilah</i> (and the Mishnah follows R. Simeon), but about blood unfit for atonement he agrees that there can be no <i>meˋilah</i>. Therefore the expression “they differ” does not refer to the Amoraim reporting in the name of R. Joḥanan, but to R. Sineon and the Sages in the Tosephta.</i>.
Rebbi Abba the son of Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba: So the Sages are answering Rebbi Simeon. If he sold them, would it not transfer sanctity to the money? What is the difference between them and their money’s worth<sup class="footnote-marker">225</sup><i class="footnote">Since anything given to the Temple for its upkeep is there to be sold and the money used for sacred purposes, the holiness of the dedicated object is transferred to the money while the object reverts to profane status. But <i>meˋilah</i>, larceny committed on <i>sacra</i>, only applies to profane use of sacred objects, not to redemptions (or to use that can be legitimized by redemption.) Therefore the distinction made by R. Simeon is not consistent with our rules.</i>? This disagrees with what Rebbi Eleazar said: There are those of them of which they said, one has no usufruct but one does not commit larceny, therefore it one sold them it does not transfer sanctity to the money, and there are those of them of which they said, one has no usufruct but one does not commit larceny, therefore if one sold them it transfers sanctity to the money. Of the ashes of the interior altar and the candelabrum one has no usufruct but one does not commit larceny, therefore if one sold them it does not transfer sanctity to the money<sup class="footnote-marker">226</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Meˋilah</i> 3:4.</i>. Of blood one has no usufruct but one does not commit larceny, therefore if one sold it, it transfers sanctity to the money.

Halakhah 7

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> All actions of the Day of Atonement which have been prescribed in their sequence<sup class="footnote-marker">227</sup><i class="footnote">The order of actions prescribed to the High Priest in <i>Lev</i>. 16 must be followed exactly.</i>, if he advanced one action to another he did not do anything. If he advanced he-goat’s blood to the bull’s blood he has to sprinkle he-goat’s blood after the bull’s blood. If the blood was spilled before he finishes all givings required in the interior<sup class="footnote-marker">228</sup><i class="footnote">In the Holiest of Holies.</i>, he has to bring other blood and starts sprinkling anew in the interior. So it is in the Temple Hall and so it is with the golden altar, since all of these are separate atonements<sup class="footnote-marker">229</sup><i class="footnote">If the blood was spilled after an action was completed, new animals and new blood only are required for the subsequent actions; one does not have to start from the beginning.</i>. Rebbi Eleazar and Rebbi Simeon are saying, he starts at the place where he interrupted<sup class="footnote-marker">230</sup><i class="footnote">While the anonymous Tanna requires the repetition of any partially complete action, R. Eleazar and R. Simeon accept completion with other blood of actions partially executed.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> It was stated:<sup class="footnote-marker">231</sup><i class="footnote">Tosephta 3:4, Babli 60a.</i> “Rebbi Jehudah said, when has this<sup class="footnote-marker">232</sup><i class="footnote">That a change in the sequence of actions invalidates the service.</i> been said? About service performed inside in white garments. But service performed outside in golden garments if he advanced one action to another, what he did is done. And the Sages are saying, even for service performed outside in golden garments if he advanced one action to another, he did not do anything.” Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan<sup class="footnote-marker">233</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 60a/b.</i>: Both of them are explaining the same verse<sup class="footnote-marker">234</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ex</i>. 30:10.</i>: <i>of the blood of the atoning sacrifice once</i>. The rabbis are saying, service which is performed one [time]<sup class="footnote-marker">235</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition, probably from the parallel in the Babli.</i> in the year. Rebbi Jehudah is saying, a place in which he enters one [time]<sup class="footnote-marker">235</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition, probably from the parallel in the Babli.</i> per year.
Rebbi Hoshaia in the name of Rebbi Ephes: About givings between the beams; but givings between the gobelins the he-goat is obstructive for the bull<sup class="footnote-marker">236</sup><i class="footnote">Chapter 4:1, Note 55.</i>. Rebbi Eleazar said, if he gave of the bull’s blood between the beams and between the gobelins and afterwards freshly slaughtered the he-goat it is qualified<sup class="footnote-marker">237</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 40a, disputing the assertion of R. Ephes.</i>. Rebbi Yose said, if the bull’s and the he-goat’s blood in the cup was spilled, would he not bring another bull and it would be qualified<sup class="footnote-marker">238</sup><i class="footnote">This cannot mean that the bull’s and the he-goat’s blood were mixed in one cup since this is scheduled only after both kinds of blood were sprinkled on the gobelins. R. Yose argues in support of R. Eleazar, since the blood in the cup could be spilled at any moment, then the slaughter can happen at any moment.</i>? What is the difference whether he slaughtered before he gave or slaughtered after he gave? If it had said “he gives” that would have been correct<sup class="footnote-marker">239</sup><i class="footnote">For the rabbis each group of sprinkling, in the Holiest of Holies, on the gobelins, and on the altar, forms a unit. If anything was incomplete or disqualifying in one of the actions, the entire action must be repeated. For R. Eleazar and R. Simeon every single sprinkling is a commandment by itself. In all there are 7+1 sprinklings of bull’s blood and the same number of he-goat’s blood in the Holiest of Holies, the same number of both kinds of blood on the gobelins, 4 of the combined blood on the horns of the golden altar and 7 on its top, for a total of 4x8+11 = 43.</i>.
The rabbis say, three for qualification and three for disqualification. Rebbi Eleazar and Rebbi Simeon are saying, 43 for qualification and 43 for disqualification<sup class="footnote-marker">239</sup><i class="footnote">For the rabbis each group of sprinkling, in the Holiest of Holies, on the gobelins, and on the altar, forms a unit. If anything was incomplete or disqualifying in one of the actions, the entire action must be repeated. For R. Eleazar and R. Simeon every single sprinkling is a commandment by itself. In all there are 7+1 sprinklings of bull’s blood and the same number of he-goat’s blood in the Holiest of Holies, the same number of both kinds of blood on the gobelins, 4 of the combined blood on the horns of the golden altar and 7 on its top, for a total of 4x8+11 = 43.</i>. Therefore the rabbis say, any seven<sup class="footnote-marker">240</sup><i class="footnote">This really should read “eight”.</i> are atonement by themselves. [Rebbi Eleazar and Rebbi Simeon are saying, each single one is atonement by itself.]<sup class="footnote-marker">241</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition.</i> Rebbi Zeˋira in the name of Rebbi Eleazar<sup class="footnote-marker">242</sup><i class="footnote">The Amora ben Pedat, not the Tanna, ben Arakh, quoted in the Tosephta.</i>, the reason of Rebbi Eleazar and<sup class="footnote-marker">243</sup><i class="footnote">Reading וְ instead of the similar sounding בֵי.</i> Rebbi Simeon: <i>he finished atoning for the holy</i><sup class="footnote-marker">244</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev</i>. 16:20.</i>, even if there is only one giving, the Torah says “he finished”<sup class="footnote-marker">245</sup><i class="footnote">Since emphasis is on finishing, even if only a single sprinkling is needed to complete the ceremony it is counted and valid.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">246</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Sifra Aḥare Parashah</i> 4(3); a minority opinion in the Babli, 61b.</i>“Rebbi Eleazar<sup class="footnote-marker">247</sup><i class="footnote">The Tanna.</i> said, if he gave part of the givings when the blood was spilled, he brings others in their place; these [and those]<sup class="footnote-marker">248</sup><i class="footnote">Addition by the corrector. While the statement is correct, the addition is questionable. As is clear from the text of <i>Sifra</i> and the remark following the quote, everybody agrees and it is obvious from the biblical text (<i>Lev</i>. 20:27) that the bull and the he-goat on whose blood the ceremony is completed have to be burned outside the city of Jerusalem and the people occupied with this burning become severely impure. The question is whether the animals whose blood was first brought into the sanctuary but was not used to finish the ceremonies, either because it was spilled or because of some disqualification, have to be disposed in the same way. This is asserted by R. Eleazar but negated by RR. Meïr and Simeon.</i> are (emptied)<sup class="footnote-marker">249</sup><i class="footnote">For “emptied” read נשרפין “burned”. If the blood was spilled, it cannot be emptied a second time.</i> following their commandments.” We need this only if an designation of disqualification was applicable to them<sup class="footnote-marker">250</sup><i class="footnote">Or if it was spilled, cf. Note 248.</i>. Rebbi Yose said, this is correct. if he gave part of the givings when the blood was spilled, he brings others in their place; and the first ones are subject to <i>meˋilah</i><sup class="footnote-marker">251</sup><i class="footnote">This is equivalent to saying that they did not completely lose their status as <i>sancta</i> and therefore have to be burned following the biblical rules.</i>. Rebbi Ḥaggai asked before Rebbi Yose, so far if he slaughtered the first ones for qualification and the second one for disqualification<sup class="footnote-marker">252</sup><i class="footnote">Disqualification not of the second but the first couple of animals. Slaughter of animals with the intent that they be disqualified makes them disqualified and removes sacral status.</i>. If he slaughtered the first ones for disqualification and the second one for qualification? Rebbi Yose said, we find that disqualification [eliminates]<sup class="footnote-marker">253</sup><i class="footnote">Necessary corrector’s addition.</i> <i>piggul</i><sup class="footnote-marker">254</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Piggul</i>(<i>Lev</i>. 19:7) is slaughter with the intent that the sacrificial meat be eaten outside its allotted time frame. Only <i>sancta</i>, parts of which may be eaten, can become <i>piggul</i>, a disqualification which prevents the meat from being eaten, automatically removes <i>piggul</i>. Mishnah <i>Zevaḥim</i> 2:3.</i>; do we find that disqualification eliminates qualification<sup class="footnote-marker">255</sup><i class="footnote">R. Ḥaggai’s question is baseless; the disqualification of the first sacrifice cannot have influence on the status of the second.</i>?

Chapter 6



Halakhah 1

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> The commandment for the two he-goats of the Day of Atonement is that they be equal in looks, in height, and in value, and be bought simultaneously. Even if they are not equal they are qualified; if one was bought one day and the other the next day<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Or any other day.</i> they are qualified. If one of them dies, if it died before he<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">The High Priest.</i> drew lots he should take a match for the second one; if it dies after he drew lots one brings two and he draws new lots for them.<br>Then he shall say if the one for Hashem<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. Chapter 4, Note 2.</i> dies, “the one for which the lot for Hashem is drawn shall be taken in its stead.<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">Since only one new he-goat is needed; the second one was taken only to satisfy the requirement that lots be drawn for any he-goat used in the service.</i>” And if the one for Azazel died, “the one for which the lot for Azazel is drawn shall be taken in its stead.” The second one shall graze until it becomes unfit, then be sold, and its proceeds used for voluntary sacrifices<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">The monies to be used to buy elevation sacrifices for times when otherwise the altar would be idle.</i> since no public purification sacrifice is allowed to die<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">In contrast to private purification sacrifices which are not used because the owner used another animal in its stead. It cannot be used for another person, cannot be redeemed, and cannot be used in any other way.</i>. Rebbi Jehudah says, it shall die. In addition, Rebbi Jehudah says, if the blood is spilled the one to be sent away shall die, if the one to be sent away dies the blood shall be spilled<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">Since R. Jehudah holds that if for any reason one of the he-goats or its blood cannot be used, the other cannot be used either and has to be let to die.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “The two he-goats of the Day of Atonement,” etc. <sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">The following is a slightly changed verson of a text appearing in <i>Sanhedrin</i> 3:10 (Notes 150–162) and <i>Ševuot</i> 4:1 (Notes 7–17).</i><i>He-goats</i><sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:5,7,8. Babli 62b, <i>Sifra Aḥare Parasḥah</i> 2(1).</i>, the minimum of he-goats are two. If so, why does it say <i>two</i>? That they be equal.
[<i>Sheep</i><sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ex</i>. 27:38, <i>Num</i>. 28:3.</i><i>,</i> the minimum of sheep are two. If so, why does it say <i>two</i>? That both be equal.]<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition from the parallel sources.</i>
<i>Birds</i><sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 14:4.</i><i>,</i> the minimum of <i>birds</i> are two. If so, why does it say <i>two</i>? That both be equal.
<i>Trumpets</i><sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Num.</i> 10:2.</i><i>,</i> the minimum of <i>trumpets</i> are two. If so, why does it say <i>two</i>? that both be equal.
Rebbi Haggai objected before Rebbi Yose. Is there not written<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Deut.</i> 19:17.</i>: <i>The two men who have the lawsuit shall stand before the Eternal?</i> Now <i>men,</i> is not two the minimum of “men”? If so, why does it say <i>two</i>? That both be equal? But it is written<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Deut.</i> 24:17.</i>: <i>Do not bend the lawsuit of the proselyte, the orphan,…</i> So we find that a proselyte can have a lawsuit against one who is not a proselyte, an orphan may have a lawsuit against one who is not an orphan, a widow against somebody who is not a widow. Then why does the verse say <i>two</i>? It is free to be combined and one may infer from it an <i>equal cut.</i> It is said here <i>two</i> and it is said there <i>two.</i> Since there <i>two</i> means men but not women nor underaged, also here <i>two</i> means men but not women nor underaged. From this we learn that a woman may not be a (judge) [witness]; consequently a woman may not be a (witness) [judge]<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">The scribe’s text in parentheses conforms to the parallels; the corrector’s in brackets is more logical.</i>.
Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun, Rebbi Ḥuna in the name of Rebbi Yose. It is said here <i>two,</i>[<i>by the mouth of two witnesses</i><sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Deut.</i> 17:6.</i>]<i>,</i> and it is said there <i>two, two men remained in the camp</i><sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Num.</i> 11:27.</i><i>.</i> Since there <i>two</i> means men but not women nor underaged, also here <i>two</i> means men but not women nor underaged. Then why is it said (<i>two</i>) [<i>and the two men shall stand</i>]<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">If actually the same price was paid for the two he-goats used on the Day of Atonement, but if they were regularly sold in the market one of them clearly would fetch a higher price, they are not disqualified but do not fulfill the biblical requirement of equality.</i>? Lest one of them be standing while the other be sitting; [one is silent while the other talks]<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition from the parallel sources.</i>, one says everything he has to say, but to the other one says, make your statement short. With one the judge is friendly, to the other he is unfriendly, lets one sit and the other stand. [They said in the name of Rebbi Ismael, one says to him, either you dress as he is dressed or pay him to be dressed as you are.]<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition from the parallel sources.</i>
Rebbi Jehudah said, I heard that if the judge wants to let both of them sit, he may tell them to sit down. What is forbidden is that one be standing and the other sitting; or that one says everything he has to say, but to the other one says, make your statement short, etc.
Rebbi Abba said in the name of Rav Ḥuna: The witnesses have to stand while testifying. Rebbi Jeremiah in the name of Rebbi Abbahu: Also the parties have to stand at the moment the testimony is delivered..
If they are equal in price but unequal in value, the he-goats are not as commanded<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">If actually the same price was paid for the two he-goats used on the Day of Atonement, but if they were regularly sold in the market one of them clearly would fetch a higher price, they are not disqualified but do not fulfill the biblical requirement of equality.</i>; equal in value but not equal in price, the he-goats are as commanded. Better in its body<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">Having more meat.</i> or better in its looks, what is preferable? Rebbi Jeremiah thought to say<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">This is the only opinion we have on the problem but it is not necessarily to be followed in practice if the Temple will be rebuilt.</i> that we may understand it from the following: Of cut greenish and dry uncut, cut greenish is preferable<sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to the <i>ˋomer,</i> the sacrifice of first barley (<i>Lev.</i> 2:14) which has to be <i>greenish grain parched with fire, peeled barley of the fresh ear.</i> While the <i>ˋomer</i> should be freshly cut, if the choice is only between cut moist or uncut completely dry barley, cut moist grain is preferable since this is explicitly required by the verse. אָבִיב is barley which is edible but still has a moist greenish tint; in Southern Germany known as <i>Grünkern.</i> Cf. Tosephta <i>Menaḥot</i> 10:33.</i>. This implies, better in its body [or better in its looks]<sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote">Corrector’s addition. It might be that the scribe’s second “better in its body” is dittography, which would make the correction unnecessary.</i>, better in its body is preferable.
So is the Mishnah: “One brings two and he draws new lots for them. He shall say, ‘the one for which the lot for Hashem is drawn shall be taken in its stead.’<sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote">As it was translated in Mishnah 2, the clause אִם שֶׁל שֵׁם מֵת “if the one for Hashem dies,” describes the background of the required action; it is not part of the declaration by the High Priest.</i>” Which of them is sacrificed first<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote">This now refers to the case that the he-goat to be sent to the Azazel dies and one is left with two he-goats as prospective sacrifices.</i>? Rav said, the second in the second pair; Rebbi Joḥanan said, the second in the first pair<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote">Rav holds that since the sacrifice of the first he-goat becomes invalidated if the he-goat for Azazel died, since it was stated that if the he-goat for the Azazel died after the first he-goat had been slaughtered, the blood has to be poured out and the entire ceremony started anew with a new pair of he-goats, a sacrifice which became invalidated never can be reinstated. While it is a general principle that a sacrifice which became invalidated never can be reinstated, R. Joḥanan holds that the living he-goat is not disqualified if its companion he-goat died, but it only is suspended. If a second he-goat is newly chosen, the suspension of the first is removed.</i>. Rebbi Zeˋira said, the reason of Rebbi Joḥanan: <i>he shall make it a purification sacrifice</i><sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:19.</i><i>,</i> of the first {pair.<sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote">Since the verse refers to the first pair, the first he-goat is irrevocably made a sacrifice.</i>} Rebbi La said, the reason of Rebbi Joḥanan: <i>he shall make it a purification sacrifice,</i> he established it for dependency lest it be pushed aside<sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote">A different formulation of the same idea.</i>. This is parallel to what Rebbi Jonah said in the name of Rebbi Zeˋira, <i>he shall make it a purification sacrifice,</i> he established it for dependency that its companion be paired with it. In Rebbi Joḥanan’s opinion, if the second in the second pair died, would the second in the first pair be pushed aside? There came Rebbi Abba, Rebbi Ḥiyya in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: then the second in the first pair already is pushed aside<sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote">If the replacement he-goat for the Azazel also died, R. Joḥanan might agree that a double suspension is equivalent to invalidation.</i>. [So much more would Rav’s reasoning be inverted? If the second in the second pair died, the second in the second pair already is pushed aside.<sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote">Addition of the corrector. The question here is different. One brings a second pair and draws lots. According to the Mishnah, the new he-goat for the Azazel is selected. If then the first he-goat dies, following Rav’s original position the second drawing of lots was made under erroneous hypotheses, and a third pair of he-goats would be needed.<br>The corrector’s source is unknown.</i>]
<sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote">Text from Chapter 5, Notes 141–143.</i> If he drew lots for three pairs<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">The High Priest.</i>, to give from one between the beams, from one on the gobelins, from one on the golden altar. Which of them is sent away? Rebbi Zeˋira said, <i>to atone on him</i>, one with whom one atones, the companion is sent away; one with whom one does not atone, the companion is not sent away. Rebbi Hila said, <i>to atone on him</i>, one with whom one completes atonement, the companion is sent away, one with whom one does not complete atonement, the companion is not sent away. In Rebbi Zeˋira’s opinion, all three are sent away. In Rebbi Hila’s opinion, only the last one is sent away.
“Since no public purification sacrifice is let to die<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">In contrast to private purification sacrifices which are not used because the owner used another animal in its stead. It cannot be used for another person, cannot be redeemed, and cannot be used in any other way.</i>. Rebbi Jehudah says, it shall die.” It is difficult for Rebbi Jehudah: does one draw lots originally to die? Rebbi Abun said, do we not find this following Rebbi Eliezer<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">It is sinful to try to replace a validly dedicated animal by an other (<i>Lev.</i> 27:10). In the case of (voluntary) well-being offerings, both animals are dedicated as well-being offerings. For obligatory offerings, two animals cannot be brought instead of one. In Mishnah <i>Temurah</i> 3:3, the majority rules that the replacement of a valid reparation offering and any of its offspring shall be put out to graze until they develop a defect which makes them unfit as sacrifices, then be sold, and the proceeds given to the Temple to be used for additional sacrifices, But R. Eliezer rules that they have to be allowed to die immediately without any benefit to the Temple. R. Jehudah as student of his father R. Illay, a student of R. Eliezer, can be presumed to follow the latter’s teachings.</i>, as Rebbi Eliezer said, they shall die? Rebbi Mana said, what you ask about Rebbi Jehudah you should ask about the Mishnah, as we have stated there<sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah <i>Temurah</i> 4:1. In case of a purification offering everybody agrees with R. Eliezer, and one of the he-goats for which lots are drawn is a purification offering.</i>, “the calf of a purification offering, and the replacement of a purification offering, and a purification offering whose owners died, shall die.” Would a person replace originally to die?

Halakhah 2

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> He came to the he-goat to be sent away and leaned on it with both his hands and confessed. And thus he was saying: “Please Hashem, they acted criminally, offended, sinned before You, Your people, the House of Israel. Please Hashem, please atone the criminal acts,” etc<sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. Chapter 4, Note 61.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Bar Qappara stated, “they acted criminally, offended, sinned,” in order not to mention the shame of Israel<sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote">In his text, the High Priest does not mention “Your people, the House of Israel.”</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Sifra Aḥare Pereq</i> 2(5),</i><i>It shall be made standing alive,</i> This teaches that in the end it will die<sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:9. Since the he-goat could not stand if he were not alive, the emphasis on “alive” in this verse implies that later it will not be alive, that it should not be let free in the desert but be thrown from a cliff.</i>. <sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote">This paragraph is a slight rewrite of a paragraph in <i>Ševuot</i> 1:10 (Notes 127–241).</i> How long must it live? Up to <i>he will finish atoning the Sanctuary</i><sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:20. Since there can be no atonement without confession, this will include the last confession of the High Priest even though it is mentioned only in v. 21.</i><i>,</i> the words of Rebbi Jehudah. Rebbi Simeon says, up to the moment of confession. In Rebbi Jehudah’s opinion, the confession is indispensable. In Rebbi Simeon’s opinion, the confession is not indispensable<sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote">It remains unresolved whether for R. Simeon no confession is obstructive or only the last one which is mentioned after the atonement of the Sanctuary was declared complete.</i>. What is the difference between them? If he sent it without a confession. In Rebbi Jehudah’s opinion, he must bring another he-goat. In Rebbi Simeon’s opinion, he does not have to bring another he-goat. The same holds for the bull. If he slaughtered without confession. In Rebbi Jehudah’s opinion, he must bring another bull. In Rebbi Simeon’s opinion, he does not have to bring another bull. If he confessed, slaughtered, then the blood was spilled. Do you say, does he have to bring another bull and confess a second time or did he do his duty with the first confession? The same holds for the scapegoat; must he cast lots a second time or did he do his duty with the first confession<sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote">It already had been stated that there has to be another drawing of lots with new animals,, the question is only about the confessions.</i>?

Halakhah 3

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> He handed him over to the one who led him. Everybody is qualified to lead him, but the High Priests made it an institution that they did not let an Israel lead him. Rebbi Yose said, it happened that Arsela<sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote">“Hammock”, a nickname.</i> from Sepphoris led it, and he was an Israel.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <i>He shall send him by a man</i><sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:21.</i><i>,</i> to qualify the non-Cohen<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote">Since “man” is unspecific. Babli 66a/b.</i>. <i>Timely</i><sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:21.</i><i>.</i> that he be ready; <i>timely,</i> that he be prepared. <i>Timely,</i> even on the Sabbath; <i>timely,</i> even in impurity. Can he be not ready but prepared<sup class="footnote-marker">46</sup><i class="footnote">Ready and prepared are practically the same, the duplication is unwarranted.</i>? But that he should not send him by two people. If he sent him by two people, does he make clothing impure<sup class="footnote-marker">47</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:26 states that the person bringing the scapegoat to the desert becomes impure together with his clothing.</i>? Let us hear from the following: <i>And the one who sends</i><sup class="footnote-marker">48</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Lev.</i> 16:26.</i>; not who was sending the one who sends. This implies that if he sent him by two people, it does not make clothing impure<sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote">Only the person first appointed to the task becomes impure.</i>.
If it escapes in the direction in which it is going, it makes clothing impure, in the opposite direction it does not make clothing impure<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 66b, Tosephta 3:14.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 66b, Tosephta 3:14.</i>“They asked Rebbi Eliezer, if the agent got sick? He said to them, so you shall be in peace. If the scapegoat fell ill? He said to them, it can carry you and me. If he pushed it but it did not die? He said to them, so it shall happen to all enemies of Heaven. Not that Rebbi Eliezer wanted to distract them, only that he did not tell them statements which he never had heard<sup class="footnote-marker">52</sup><i class="footnote">Which probably means that the cases never had happened before during the ascendancy of the Pharisees in the Temple service.</i>. But the Sages are saying, if the agent got sick, he<sup class="footnote-marker">53</sup><i class="footnote">The High Priest.</i> sends it<sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">The scapegoat.</i> by somebody else/ If the scapegoat fell ill, he<sup class="footnote-marker">55</sup><i class="footnote">The designated agent.</i> lets it<sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">The scapegoat.</i> be carried on a donkey. If he<sup class="footnote-marker">55</sup><i class="footnote">The designated agent.</i> pushed it<sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">The scapegoat.</i> but it did not die, he<sup class="footnote-marker">55</sup><i class="footnote">The designated agent.</i> has to descend after it and kill it.”
<sup class="footnote-marker">56</sup><i class="footnote">Babli 39a, Tosephta <i>Soṭah</i> 13:6–8.</i>“All during Simeon the Just’s lifetime he<sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">The scapegoat.</i> did not fall down half the mountain before he dissolved into limbs; after Simeon the Just’s death he fled to the desert and was eaten by the Saracens. All during Simeon the Just’s lifetime the lot for Hashem<sup class="footnote-marker">57</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah 4:1.</i> came up in his right hand; after Simeon the Just’s death sometimes it came up to the right, sometimes to the left. All during Simeon the Just’s lifetime the Easternmost light<sup class="footnote-marker">58</sup><i class="footnote">In the evening, the easternmost light of the candelabrum was lit first but in the morning it was serviced last. It was one of the miracles of the Temple that it outlasted all other lights of the candelabrum.</i> was burning; after Simeon the Just’s death sometimes it was extinguished, sometimes burning. All during Simeon the Just’s lifetime the shiny strip<sup class="footnote-marker">59</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah 6.</i> turned white; after Simeon the Just’s death sometimes it turned white, sometimes it turned red. All during Simeon the Just’s lifetime the fire on the altar steadily increased; after they had put on two logs in the morning<sup class="footnote-marker">60</sup><i class="footnote">Chapter 2, Note 19.</i> they did not add anything during the day. After Simeon the Just’s death the fire weakened; the had to add wood all day long.
